Current Commentary

A Glimmer of Hope in the Declining Silk Industry

— Liu

Silk sales, since the overseas market was seized, are now merely sustained by domestic users. However, in recent years, although the price of silk has been falling, sales are still not as good as before. As a result, silk businesses, whether weaving or trading, are all at risk of losses. It is heard that the market has become even worse since this year. The reason is that, no matter how cheap the selling price is, business is still difficult to improve. This is because the general economic hardship is becoming increasingly acute. No matter how beautiful the goods are, no matter how cheap the price is, it is useless because people cannot afford to buy them. Cheapness is also useless. This price decline is due to a reduction in demand. The situation of cheap prices due to reduced demand is very different from that of cheap prices due to overproduction. Therefore, it is feared that the silk industry will not improve easily, and the silk market will not recover in a short period of time. Since it is not a short-term matter, should we let it decline without taking any measures to save it? That is not the case either. China's greatest economic difficulty today lies in non-production. If there is no production, there is no source of income, and the way out is blocked. Silk is ultimately a productive industry. How can we not raise silkworms because the price of silk is low? If this is the case, there is no way to produce, and how can the market have any hope of improving? Therefore, today's question is, what is the policy for this year's cocoon harvest? What are the measures for silk reeling after the cocoon harvest? For farmers, they should not stop raising silkworms because the price of cocoons is low. Although the price of cocoons is low, there is still income after all, which is better than non-production. For cocoon merchants, in the past, there was no lack of suppressing silkworm farmers when collecting cocoons, hoping to obtain extraordinary profits. Or they did not distinguish between good and bad quality, which led to the destruction of the heart of improving the quality of cocoons. Or there was competition among peers, raising prices to buy, which caused the failure in the future. All of these are not correct. Cocoon merchants themselves should also bear considerable responsibility for the degradation of cocoon quality and the failure of the past cocoon industry. The silk reeling industry should start from refreshing technology and improving production equipment. This is difficult, but without doing so, it will not be possible to compete in the overseas market, and recovery will be even more difficult. The habit of waiting for prices to estimate, ignoring the situation, and only considering self-interest also needs to be reformed. The silk industry has been renovating and innovating in recent years, competing for novelty and beauty, which is enough to move people's eyes and prevent the intrusion of foreign goods. However, precisely because of this, in the autumn of economic tightening and depression of all industries, the market is not enough to cope with frequent renovations. Inventory is easy to be left on the shelves, and turnover loses its agility. Losses then follow. Therefore, it seems that the silk industry should seek its own control, both for production and sales. If it can be consistent in valuing quality over quantity and agreeing not to endorse foreign goods, it will be a way to save itself and the silk cocoon industry. Today, if we want to reduce the number of import excesses, in addition to actively promoting exports, we must seek self-use in self-produced goods and not rely on external demand. In this way, foreign goods will have no way to be imported. Therefore, while maintaining the silk industry, the silk industry strives to strengthen itself, examines past mistakes, and tries to improve from all aspects to meet the needs of the Chinese people. This is the best way to produce and use for oneself.

German Air Minister Göring's Speech

The German Air Force Should be Equal to France's, Denies Violating International Treaties

(Berlin) German Air Minister General Göring, when speaking today about Germany's air defense and its wishes, firmly denied that Germany intended to violate international treaties, saying that Germany's air defense is equal to that of any country in the world, and its defense power should be as strong as the combined offensive power of other countries. Germany's special need is that its air force should be equal to the French air force. If there are international treaties that include all countries, then Germany will definitely abide by them and reduce its air force. Since Germany's rearmament, Germany has taken several concrete actions for peace. Judging from Göring's remarks regarding the wishes of the German air force, his meaning seems to be that if the European powers, excluding Germany, have a joint defense organization, then Germany will demand to have an air force as strong as the combined air forces of other countries. However, the signing of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact cannot be interpreted as Germany needing an air force equal in strength to the combined forces of France and Russia, because Russia should not be considered a European country. (Reuters, 2nd)

(Berlin) According to reliable sources today, new recruits will receive one year of training in accordance with the newly promulgated military service law. This measure is scheduled to be implemented from October 1st. In addition, special training for air force and motor vehicle units, their service regulations will be stipulated separately. (Reuters, 3rd)

Communication Cut Off in Manila, Communist Uprising in the Philippines, Hundreds Killed and Injured in Midnight Uprising, Military and Police Suppress the Riot and Gradually Restore Order

(Manila) The Communist Party of the Philippines suddenly launched an uprising in various areas near Manila last night. After military and police suppression, the riot gradually subsided this morning. At dawn today, Manila dispatched reinforcements to the riot locations. Most of the rebels have now been routed. Manila residents were initially very frightened upon hearing the news of the Communist Party attacking the capital. After learning that communication between the capital and the provinces had been cut off and that Manila was isolated, they became even more anxious. The troops immediately went on the defensive to prevent further unrest. The number of dead and wounded is now known to be as follows: Laguna Province, 54 dead, 64 wounded; Cavite, number of dead unknown, 3 wounded; Bulacan, 3 dead, 12 wounded. The highest number of casualties occurred in Cabuyao, where 47 rebels were killed, 55 wounded, and many arrested. Military and police casualties were very light, with only 1 killed and 10 wounded. Rumors in Washington suggested that Japan provided financial assistance to the Communist uprising. The Japanese Consul in Manila today firmly denied this, saying that nothing could be more absurd. The Chinese Consul is extremely concerned about this riot. Vice Consul Mr. Mo inquired with the police department this afternoon and said that there were rumors that the communists were planning to rob Chinese shops. The authorities assured him that security was tight and that the Chinese in Manila need not be alarmed. The news of the Communist uprising reached here at 8:30 last night. Shortly after, communications were cut off. The authorities immediately dispatched military and police to various locations. In the early morning, the military and police arrived in Cabuyao and launched an attack on the Communist Party's concentration point. The rebels resisted stubbornly, not only refusing to surrender but also opening fire. The military and police then launched a forceful assault on the church occupied by the rebels. After a fierce battle lasting over an hour, 47 rebels were killed and the rest scattered. One wounded rebel claimed that he had been persuaded to join the demonstration and never expected it to turn into a battle. Another captured rebel said that he heard that the Communist leader, Ramos, had returned from Japan by plane. Many of the captured rebels carried amulets, believing that these amulets could protect their bodies from harm. The Communist Party is quite popular among workers. Due to the recent economic recession and the hardships faced by workers, many have joined the Communist Party. This riot was clearly planned in advance, taking advantage of the fact that the acting governor was not in Manila, launching attacks in various locations. This afternoon, government officials stated that the riot in Cabuyao had failed and that the unrest in other areas could be considered pacified. The Manila military authorities are prepared to dispatch troops at any time. (Reuters, 3rd)

US Senator Hopes the Disturbance Will Pass Quickly

(Washington) Today, Republican Senator Gibson stated that he had received hints of serious disturbances brewing in the Philippines a week ago. Mr. Gibson said, "I hope the current disturbance will pass quickly, and the Filipinos should know that in these turbulent times in the East, they need the assistance of a powerful nation." In Washington, Philippine Resident Commissioner de Guia, upon receiving news of the uprising, explained that the disturbance may only be an outbreak by a few misguided Filipinos, or the result of incitement by cunning individuals exploiting the public. Governor General Murphy and Senate President Quezon both believe that this disturbance does not represent the true sentiment of the Filipino people. Democrat Kim William said that this rebellion may be the work of a few radicals. The majority of Filipinos are law-abiding and will not participate in such demonstrations. At most, some people are disappointed by the delayed approval of independence, which is understandable, but most Filipinos can approach this matter with good spirit. (National Telegram, 2nd)

US Sailors Ordered to Defend the Navy Yard

Manila - Santa Rosa, Luzon, became a battlefield today. A thousand radicals armed with weapons suddenly attacked the town and seized the city hall, but were eventually driven back by the military and police. As a result, five people were killed and eight wounded. Residents were terrified and afraid to leave their homes. It is reported that 300 armed rebels in Cavite province are brewing unrest. US sailors have been ordered to defend the Cavite Navy Yard. The city hall of San Ildefonso, Bulacan, was also occupied by rebels. The police were surrounded for several hours. After a fierce battle, the police finally defeated the rebels, killing six of them. (Reuters, 2nd)

Circumstances of the Riot, All Leaders Wanted

Manila - Today, over ten villages and cities near Manila were devastated by a brutal riot by radical farmers. According to information received this afternoon, approximately fifty to sixty people have died, and over fifty have been injured. The swift action of the police preserved the Philippine capital from being affected by the "Sakdalistas." Telephone and telegraph lines within a ten-to-fifteen-mile radius of Manila have been cut, making communication with the disturbed areas impossible. Among the dead, at least one was a local official who was killed when a group of police officers were ambushed and shot. It is reported that fully armed rebels came from the provinces of Laguna, Rizal, Bulacan, and Cavite. The Philippine newspaper The Tribune reported that a police team of over one hundred attacked the rebels in Cabuyao, killing approximately sixty and wounding over forty. Later, the official wireless report received by the Police Headquarters, issued by Colonel Nick Taulto, stated that Cabuyao had been recaptured, with forty-seven rebels killed and countless captured. The assault on Calamba is ongoing, but there is a great need for ammunition and rifle bullets. The earliest news of the riot received by the police station came from the underworld at eight o'clock last night. The news stated that the rioters planned to attack Manila at midnight. Troops rushed to the affected areas to suppress the riotous farmers and agitators. The garrison in Santa Rosa, Laguna, was ambushed and fought hand-to-hand with the rebels. An officer was killed, and six were injured. Two "Sakdalistas" were killed, and two children were injured. At least four rebels were captured. The next riot occurred in San Ildefonso, Bulacan, where rebels forcibly occupied the municipal government building. Riots also occurred in other towns such as San Jose, Daniel Monte, Binangonan, Dasmariñas, Tanza, Bacoor, Silang, Santa Rosa, and Biñan. An order has been issued for the arrest of Marino Enage, the representative of Laguna province in the Philippine legislature, who was elected in 1934 as the leader of the "Sakdalista" party, but it is rumored that he later left the party. Other leaders are also wanted in order to investigate the riot. (National Telegram, 3rd)

The Cause of the Rebellion Seems to be Opposition to the Constitution

(New York) News from the Philippines received here today states that the rebellion near Manila was likely caused by opponents of the Philippine Constitution. Philippine Senate President Quezon, currently in New York, stated this afternoon that telegraph and telephone communication between Manila and the provinces had been cut off. According to a Manila newspaper, demonstrations occurred in five provinces. The Philippine Constitution, approved by President Roosevelt on March 23, stipulates a Philippine republican system, recognizes American sovereignty, and requires officials to swear allegiance to the United States upon the establishment of the republic on December 30. The Philippine Congress is scheduled to vote on it on May 11. (Reuters, 2nd)

Danzig Currency Devaluation, Reduced by Forty-Two Percent, Aimed at Increasing Trade

(Berlin) The Danzig City Government has devalued the Gulden by forty-two percent. The general interpretation is that this should have happened long ago. Only with the assistance of the German Central Bank was the Bank of Danzig able to temporarily overcome the difficulties. However, the Central Bank is now unable to continue its assistance. In general, German assistance was only enough to delay the devaluation until after the Free City Council elections, so that the Nazi Party's election campaign would not be affected. The main reasons for the devaluation are as follows: (1) The Nazi City Government's efforts to prevent unemployment have led to a gradual decrease in the gold reserves and cash of the Danzig Bank. In 1933, the gold reserves amounted to 40,000,000 Gulden, which decreased to 21,000,000 Gulden in March of this year. On the other hand, the amount of bills payable also increased from 14,000,000 to 24,000,000 Gulden. (2) The maritime transport business of the Polish port of Gdynia is becoming increasingly developed, resulting in fierce competition with the port of Danzig. In addition, the advance capital for transit trade also poses a great difficulty to the cash situation. The Free City's foreign claims are mostly long-term, and therefore affected by the devaluation of the currencies of many countries, but its foreign debts are mostly short-term. Therefore, the City Government was able to勉力维持戈爾盾之匯率以至今日者,賴有德國之資助耳 maintain the exchange rate of the Gulden until today, thanks to German funding. This morning, the City Government issued a bulletin, denouncing the public's credit panic, saying that it was a political strategy of the opposition party, and tantamount to rebellious behavior. Now that the exchange rate of the Gulden has fallen to half that of the Mark, the economic relations between the Free City and Germany have been hindered by the devaluation. Conversely, the exchange rate of the Gulden is roughly equivalent to the Polish currency Zloty, and the economic relations between the two sides should become closer as a result. (Havas, 2nd)

Crowded Shops

Warsaw - After the Senate of the Free City of Danzig decided to reduce the value of the Danzig currency, the Gulden, by forty-two percent, residents of the Free City rushed to various shops with banknotes to purchase goods. The shops were extremely crowded. As a result, some shops temporarily closed, while others limited the quantity of goods sold. This afternoon, the Danzig City Council held a meeting, attended by Senate President Greiser, who explained that the Senate's sudden decision to devalue the currency was intended to avoid speculation. The purpose of the devaluation is to reduce imports and increase exports. Because Danzig is restricted by the Treaty of Versailles, which deprives it of its natural market, it is now forced to devalue the currency in order to revive Danzig's trade. (Havas, 2nd)

Brazil Agrees to Participate in the Mediation of the Gran Chaco Dispute

Brazilian Capital - Recently, the United States, Argentina, Chile, and Peru jointly invited Brazil to participate in the mediation of the Gran Chaco dispute. The governments of Great Britain, France, and Italy also strongly urged Brazil to accept this invitation. It is now known that the Brazilian government has accepted this invitation and has notified the British, French, and Italian ambassadors to Brazil, expressing its hope to unite collective forces to guarantee lasting peace on the American continent and to ensure that the conflict between Bolivia and Paraguay is resolved fairly. (Havas, 2nd)

British House of Commons Debates Foreign Policy: MacDonald Delivers Manifesto, Advocating Cooperation with Germany to Maintain European Peace; Britain Unwilling to Participate in Central European Rome Conference

(London) Today, the House of Commons debated foreign policy. The diplomatic gallery and the public gallery were full. Prime Minister MacDonald delivered a manifesto, strongly advocating cooperation with Germany to maintain peace and limit armaments, especially in the air. Foreign Secretary Simon also made a similar appeal, urging Germany to show its willingness to participate in peace efforts, not only in words but also in deeds. Commerce Secretary Runciman announced that in 1934, Britain had shipped 96 aircraft engines manufactured in Britain to Germany, which attracted much attention. Opposition Labour Party leader Lansbury expressed extreme disappointment with the Prime Minister's manifesto. This is the general outline of today's debate. Prime Minister MacDonald stated that Britain's foreign policy combines defense, collective security, international armaments, and peace treaties. Its purpose is not military alliances but the broadest possible cooperation. Currently, attention is focused on a good understanding between Britain and

A Guarantee of Peace, and we welcome other countries to join this free alliance. The future contains opportunities for easing tensions but also contains perceptible dangers. I say this with great conviction and because I deeply understand the crux of the matter. Britain is always mindful of assisting opportunities for agreements arising from negotiations without disturbing the peace of Europe or the world. The Prime Minister then recounted the events since February 3rd, referring to the joint Anglo-French declaration issued that day, stating that one of the purposes of the planned negotiations was to conclude a free-negotiation armament treaty with Germany and other countries, replacing the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. If this had succeeded earlier, the current danger in Europe would have been more than halved. The London Declaration clearly indicated that Britain and France would break away from the confines of Versailles and establish friendly relations in Europe based on security and

Free Negotiation. On February 3rd, the British and French governments began patiently working to restore goodwill in Europe. Other governments felt that the future was gradually becoming brighter. Before long, Germany accepted the London Declaration as a basis for discussion. Consequently, their hopes were further consolidated. Then, the German government suddenly announced its intention to implement compulsory military service and immediately began increasing its peacetime military strength to 150,000 men and establishing an air force. This is truly regrettable. Historians must study the trends of events, while politicians have no choice but to deal with the real situation practically and objectively and maintain calm common sense. Should they abandon the attempt to build general trust and European peace or rely on the unity of full military power that can never save them from war? Politicians must now choose one of the two. When considering the future, they should know that Hitler has said that while he is determined not to sign treaties he considers unenforceable, he is also determined not to make

Attempts at Destruction. Hitler also publicly announced Germany's readiness and determination to accept the spirit and letter of the Locarno Treaty. This must also be noted. The declaration of February 3rd was satisfying to all of Europe because this document could be the starting point for a stable solution in Europe. The Stresa Conference did not change the substance of that declaration. The communiqué issued at the end of the Stresa Conference fully confirmed the points contained in the London communiqué. This kind of earnest statement is extremely important. The London Declaration contained suggestions for ending certain anxieties in Central and Eastern Europe. Britain is not directly affected by this suggestion but will pay attention to it or any changes to it, in the hope of providing beneficial and friendly advice at any time and obtaining the hoped-for results. Therefore, negotiations should be conducted with the concept of producing truly effective results. Regarding Central Europe, the Italian government proposed convening a meeting of the relevant governments in Rome, including Germany, to discuss a plan. The British government does not wish to send a delegation to participate in this meeting because the British government has stated that it does not wish to accept any new responsibilities regarding this matter. However, it will send personnel to

Attend as Observers in order to closely monitor the progress of the discussions and make beneficial and appropriate contributions. As for Central Europe, Germany can make valuable contributions to the security system in that region. When British Foreign Secretary Simon visited Berlin, the German leader announced that in principle, he was willing to negotiate multilateral non-aggression pacts with the countries of Eastern Europe. While countries hope that Germany is prepared to join a broader treaty, Hitler's proposal should not be allowed to fade away. Countries are convinced that Germany itself will immediately take concrete steps to advance the principles set by its leader. Why cannot this kind of non-aggression pact be compatible with the mutual guarantee pact that France and other governments have not yet negotiated? I believe the two agreements can complement each other and move towards creating a complete system of collective security in Eastern Europe. What I now wish to state is that, as far as the British government is concerned, we have never believed that the security system proposed in the London Declaration can be completed without Germany's participation. When the Stresa Conference studied the entire declaration, the policy adopted by the British government representative was to maintain the possibility of this kind of cooperation. All activities embody the principle of collective security, but the methods may occasionally differ. The general attitude of the British government is to advocate discussing the issue with a spirit of flexibility and freedom, in order to achieve this principle as much as possible and effectively

Deter Aggression. We are striving to build an instrument of cooperation and goodwill, and when Germany also makes a corresponding contribution, Berlin's sudden unilateral declaration regarding the army, air force, and navy will inevitably profoundly disturb the peace in the minds of all of Europe. This is an undeniable fact. The British government is always attentive to the various beneficial constructions proposed in Berlin and elsewhere. However, they should know that the concept of mutual trust must first be restored before detailed international negotiations can achieve full effectiveness. The instructions we brought to the Stresa Conference were not to reject any country from participating in future negotiations along the lines set out in the London Declaration due to previous incidents. The Stresa Conference did not invalidate any point of that declaration. We deeply regret the changes that have occurred in the situation, but the main purpose of that declaration remains the current goal of British foreign policy. If the trust that now exists between France, Italy, and Britain is once weakened or extinguished, the consequences will be unimaginable. We should be extremely careful to avoid this. Our goal is to increase the number of cooperating countries and try in every way to prevent them from dividing into several groups and confronting each other. Will Germany now not return and prove its willingness to help restore the international trust that its recent independent actions regarding armaments have damaged? The British government deeply feels that

International Cooperation is the only foundation on which world peace can be built. The Prime Minister then mentioned the preliminary discussions on naval affairs that will be held with German representatives in London, saying that it is truly appalling that Germany suddenly announced its shipbuilding program at this time, with submarines also included. This matter cannot be regarded as unrelated to Britain. The needs of the British Navy cannot be determined solely by domestic waters. The British Navy has extraordinary responsibilities of a global nature. I do not wish to downplay the seriousness of Germany's decision to build submarines, but the British government is still prepared to receive German representatives to open preliminary naval talks. These talks will proceed under the same conditions as the talks with the United States and Japan. Regarding the British Air Force, Lord President of the Council Baldwin has previously stated that Britain will never allow its air force to be inferior to Germany's, no matter what. The expansion of the German air force has

The extent has far exceeded the number previously estimated by the British House of Commons. The British government is now working to continue accelerating the expansion of the air force within this year to fulfill Baldwin's declaration. Regarding the Sky Pact, we are determined not to be swayed by the idea of an aggressive military alliance. We are currently seeking to conclude a defensive unity against attacks with various countries, including Germany, to protect civilians. Labour Party, i.e., Opposition Leader Lansbury, then rose to express

Extreme Disappointment because it excessively involves the increase of armaments and takes this as the initial stage of seeking other conditions for peace. At the same time, he also said that Germany's actions to rearm and the attitude it took when negotiations were about to begin are unforgivable. Labour Party members believe that Hitler's attitude has lost much sympathy. Samuel, the leader of the Liberal Party, then rose to declare that Germany's military policy is not to seek equality with other countries but to surpass them. Germany's naval proposal is untimely. Germany is also building a huge air force at an extremely rapid rate. Germany should know that if it pursues this policy without seeking a compromise on arms limitation, it will arouse public anger in all parts of Britain. If the Liberal Party studies the government's detailed proposals and knows that the British Air Force is indeed inferior to Germany's, then the Liberal Party is unwilling to bear the responsibility of allowing Britain to be in this state and will support the urgently needed plan. The next speaker was Churchill, who expressed his approval of the government's recent policies, but said that the government should have taken this action earlier. The government has been negligent in its awareness of Germany's air force armaments and has received false intelligence. The number of military aircraft currently being built in Germany is

Ten Times that of Britain. By the end of this year, the German Air Force will be at least three or four times stronger than Britain's. If Germany is the only country that needs to be dealt with, then Britain should let it do as it pleases. However, Britain, acting in concert with France, Italy, and other countries that earnestly wish to maintain peace, has the power to maintain tranquility and freedom. When countries are willing to work under the authority of the League of Nations, he does not wish to reject the cooperation of any country's government that meets this test. This has not closed the door to treaty revisions but is a plan to lay the foundation for tranquility and security. Now, tranquility and security must be established first, and then this kind of treaty revision study can begin. After Churchill finished speaking, former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain rose to comment on Germany's attitude, saying that if Germany refuses to attend when invited by other countries, then it cannot complain about being surrounded. If Germany has the spirit of cooperation and the will for peace, it will certainly be welcomed. However, if Germany does not wish to join the ranks of nations and insists on pursuing its ambitions, then it will see Britain standing in its path. (The audience cheered.) When Germany, with its vast freedom and autonomous regions, encounters Britain, comprising its four countries, it will see that the power of one country will once again surpass it. Foreign Secretary Simon then spoke to conclude the debate, saying that the British government's armaments memorandum had stipulated a plan aimed at achieving the complete abolition of naval and military aircraft. The speed at which Germany manufactures aircraft is indeed far beyond what British officers had thought. Therefore, the estimates submitted to the House of Commons in October and January of last year are not reliable. Hitler had declared to him that Germany was already equal to Britain, meaning that Germany's first-line strength was equal to Britain's first-line strength. Including overseas forces, Britain's first line has approximately 800 aircraft. Throughout the discussions in Berlin, Hitler expressed Germany's attitude sincerely and thoroughly. He strongly advocated that Germany should return to the League of Nations. However, Hitler's attitude had many disappointing aspects. Simon then mentioned Hitler's objections, saying that Hitler had argued that Japan had already withdrawn from the League of Nations and should not continue to administer the former German colonies as a mandate. He then told him that the issue of allocating mandated territories was not a matter for individual member states alone but should be handled by the League of Nations. At this point, Austen Chamberlain rose to speak in opposition, saying that the countries had never intended that the League of Nations had the power to transfer mandated territories from one country to another. Simon replied that he did not believe he had conveyed a misleading impression. Eden and he had clearly stated that the issue of transferring mandated territories could not be discussed. Hitler should not have misunderstood this. Now, in a spirit of friendship, he had reminded Germany that it had signed the five-nation declaration of equality in the security system and asked whether it was "prepared to restore the security that its recent actions had severely damaged." Simon concluded by saying, "We now urge Germany to show not only in words but also in deeds that it is prepared to do this." The debate was then adjourned. (Reuters, 2nd)

(London) After Prime Minister MacDonald announced in the House of Commons yesterday that the government would accelerate the expansion of the air force, the newspapers all welcomed it this morning. The newspapers mostly focused on the effect of the consensus among the parties on accepting the government's new air force policy. The five-year program to expand the air force, which was set in July of last year, will be implemented as soon as possible. Subsequently, expansions will be continued as necessary, depending on the situation of the German Air Force. Members of the House of Commons who are concerned about the air force issue estimate that Britain still needs to add 312 aircraft to match the strength of the German Air Force. In addition to the 20 million pounds required for the five-year program, an additional 13 million pounds will be needed. (Reuters, 3rd)

French Foreign Minister and Russian Ambassador Initial Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact; Full Text in Five Articles Published Last Night; Czech-Soviet Union to Conclude Similar Agreement; Moscow Celebrates Diplomatic Victory

(Paris) Negotiations on the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact have been completed. The pact was initialed at 6:00 PM today by Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Ambassador to France Potemkin. The pact consists of five articles (the text of which was published by Le Petit Parisien, see yesterday's telegram) and one protocol. In accordance with Articles 10, 15, 16, and 17 of the League of Nations Covenant, if there is a risk of aggression, the two contracting parties, France and the Soviet Union, have an obligation to consult each other. If, without provocation, they are subjected to aggression, then the two countries should immediately implement mutual assistance. The full text of the pact will be published tomorrow night. After signing, Laval issued a declaration, saying, "What we never forget is to participate in the security organization. We adhere to the scope of the League of Nations Covenant. From the beginning of negotiations until now, we ensure that all countries have the opportunity to join. In a word, we are working for peace only." At the same time, Potemkin declared, "This pact not only makes the relationship between France and the Soviet Union more solid but also has more important significance, because it is of great benefit to European security. However, it goes without saying that the mutual assistance pact is not targeted at any country. The Soviet Union has always believed that the obligations contained in the pact can be extended and should be extended so that other countries that sincerely love peace can join." Laval is now scheduled to depart for Russia on the ninth of this month for a visit. He will stop in Warsaw en route to hold talks with the Polish authorities. (Havas, 2nd)

(Paris) The Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Agreement was signed today by French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Ambassador to France Potemkin at the Foreign Ministry. A communiqué was issued stating that the agreement has five articles, based on Articles 10, 15, and 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, stipulating mutual assistance in the event of unprovoked aggression. The purpose of this agreement is to confirm the articles of the League of Nations Covenant and the effectiveness of the recommendations of the League of Nations Council. This responsibility is in maintaining European peace and is fully consistent with the responsibilities previously undertaken by the two countries. It also does not diminish the possibility of either the French or Soviet governments participating in regional agreements with mutual consent, as the conclusion of regional agreements is still necessary. Laval and Potemkin each made speeches, both saying that this agreement is part of the European security organization and is not directed against any country. According to Reuters Geneva, the signing of this agreement is welcomed by all those involved with the League of Nations because this agreement, within the framework of the League of Nations Covenant, is sufficient to consolidate the collective security system. People in Geneva expect that the Czech government will immediately conclude a similar agreement with Soviet Russia. It is also expected that Italy and Soviet Russia will initiate similar negotiations. (Reuters, 2nd)

Dancing in the Streets, National Acclaim

(Moscow) The news of the signing of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Agreement was greeted with great joy here. It is regarded as the most important success of Soviet Russia in international diplomacy. The public gathered in teams to parade in celebration and danced in the streets. This was first seen after the 1917 revolution. Moscow lit up with lights to celebrate. Around the portraits of Stalin and other important figures, there were thousands of electric lights, forming congratulatory messages to celebrate the victory of Soviet Russian diplomacy. The whole country is very satisfied with the current position of Soviet Russia. (Reuters, 2nd)

Italy and Poland Express Satisfaction

(Rome) The Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact was initialed last night. Here, the pact is considered to be compatible with Central European security and not contradictory to it. Great satisfaction is expressed. In addition, the Polish government has already decided to participate in the Danube Nine-Nation Conference to be held next month. The Italian side is also very relieved because Italy had some concerns about Poland's closeness to Germany, which can now be dispelled. (Havas, 3rd)

Warsaw: The Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact has been initialed in Paris but has not yet been published. Generally, people here express satisfaction because what Poland feared was that this pact would have a mechanical application and put Poland out of consideration. On the contrary, since this pact does not endanger the Franco-Polish alliance nor hinder the Russo-Polish non-aggression pact, Poland has no reason for its doubts. (Havas, 3rd)

Western Border Security Not Impaired

(Berlin) A certain important person in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a declaration regarding the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact, saying, "The obligations contained in the Locarno Pact are not affected." It was also said that the mutual assistance pact does not impair the security of Germany's western border, and the French government's respect for other international obligations is indeed the truth. (Havas, 2nd)

World Silver Prices Plunge; U.S. Senators Criticize, Demanding Treasury Immediately Purchase Silver to Break Bear Speculators Depressing Market Prices

(Washington) Senator Thomas, due to the sharp drop in world silver prices, stated in Congress today that the Treasury Department had failed to fulfill the clauses of the Silver Purchase Act, causing the silver price to fall. Other silver-supporting senators also demanded that the Treasury immediately purchase silver. Senator McCarran said that the response to the low silver price should be for the Treasury to immediately raise the silver price to $1.29 and break the bear speculators depressing market prices. Senator Adams stated that although the Treasury had to temporarily suspend silver purchases at times of market instability to prevent speculators from creating bizarre prices, the situation has now cleared up. Market fluctuations were long expected. Today's price drop is not enough to alarm people. The government not only has a reason to purchase silver, but it also has a responsibility to purchase silver now. Senator Wheeler said that the Treasury should now proceed to maintain the upward trend of silver prices. Senator King pointed out that the low silver price was due to speculation, saying that the Treasury wanted to proceed gradually, but the result was to create a situation in which speculators raised prices too quickly to seek their own profits. (Reuters, 2nd)

U.S. Chamber of Commerce Convention Criticizes Control Policies; Demands Economic Recovery Regulations Be Adopted Voluntarily by Each Industry

(Washington) President Roosevelt recently consulted with the Senate and the House of Representatives to pass a banking law to subject the Federal Reserve Bank and the entire banking organization to government control. Recently, the National Chamber of Commerce Convention passed a resolution criticizing this policy. The convention also demanded that economic recovery regulations be adopted voluntarily by each industry and not imposed. In addition, in December of last year, the House of Representatives passed the bill introduced by Representative (blank) Gagner, which stipulates that labor-management disputes should be resolved by compulsory arbitration. On the 19th of last month, the House also passed the unemployment and old-age insurance bill. All of these were attacked by the convention. Secretary of State Hull, on the other hand, defended the government's current policies, saying that those who create difficulties for the government out of concern for private interests are unwelcome. (Havas, 2nd)

Japanese Cabinet Convenes Meeting of Local Governors; Opened Yesterday at the Prime Minister's Residence; Hirota Strongly Advocates Sino-Japanese Cooperation

At the outset, Prime Minister Okada gave instructions, the gist of which was: It is my desire to gather with all of you and express my beliefs, state the government's policies, and clarify the path of public service. In this autumn of many events and many difficulties, the sincerity of dedicating oneself to the Imperial Throne and serving the people is the essence of our national polity and the foundation of our nation-building. I deeply hope that everyone will base themselves on this great righteousness and make no mistakes. The government is preparing to establish the Cabinet Deliberation Council and the Investigation Bureau to meet the demands of the times. I believe that this can overcome the drawbacks of being limited to partial views and determine an appropriate direction from the overall situation of political consultation. The Empire's position in the world will be further enhanced from this, which is very gratifying. The government will work harder to promote friendly relations with other countries and practice good faith and neighborliness. The current situation and prospects of rural villages, fishing villages, small and medium-sized commercial and industrial enterprises are not optimistic, so I hope that we will uphold the fundamental meaning of national renewal and work even harder. The date of the election for prefectural and county council members is also approaching. I hope that everyone will work hard to realize the rectification of discipline. Then, Foreign Minister Hirota, Finance Minister Takahashi, and Justice Minister Ohara each instructed on the beliefs and policies of the current cabinet. At 4:00 PM, they received instructions from Minister of the Imperial Household Yuasa at the Ministry of the Imperial Household. At 6:00 PM, they attended a dinner party at the Prime Minister's residence. (Dentsu, 3rd)

(Tokyo) The National Conference of Local Governors opened at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 3rd at the Prime Minister's residence. Japanese Foreign Minister Proposes Establishment of Sino-Japanese Chamber of Commerce Council; Organized by Industrialists from Both Countries; Established Separately in Shanghai and Osaka

(Tokyo) In light of the report from Ambassador to China Ariyoshi and the recent progress in Sino-Japanese relations, Foreign Minister Hirota increasingly believes that Sino-Japanese cooperation must start with economic cooperation. After Ambassador Ariyoshi returns to his post, he will immediately begin actively promoting Sino-Chinese economic cooperation. As for the concrete strategies, he is considering various methods, such as setting up a loan credit system, establishing joint ventures, and providing technical assistance. However, in order to implement these strategies, sufficient understanding must first be carried out between Sino-Japanese industrialists. It has now been internally determined that the first step is to advise Sino-Japanese industrialists to set up a Sino-Japanese Chamber of Commerce Council. This council will be modeled after the organizations of the Anglo-Japanese and Japan-U.S. councils and will be organized by committees from both countries in Osaka and Shanghai. After the council is established, it will naturally aim to maintain close contact between the two sides, maintain Sino-Japanese trade relations, and promote friendly relations. (Dentsu, 3rd)

(Tokyo) Recently, Chinese merchants' trade with Japan has gradually improved. Foreign Minister Hirota believes that the Chinese authorities have the intention of Sino-Japanese economic cooperation and that the time has come to promote economic relations between the two countries. He has decided to change the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' traditional trade and economic policy and plans to organize an economic committee by Sino-Japanese business circles to actively promote the development of the economies of the two countries. (United Press, 3rd)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota's plan to organize the Sino-Japanese Economic Committee has been reported in previous telegrams. Regarding matters such as Sino-Japanese joint ventures, assisting the development of Chinese industries, and developing Sino-Japanese trade, the Foreign Minister hopes for the active involvement of Sino-Japanese private-sector industrialists. The Sino-Japanese Economic Committee, which will guide this movement, will be established separately in Osaka and Shanghai. The Japanese side will proceed with preparations, with the Osaka Chamber of Commerce and Industry as the center. (United Press, 3rd)

Japanese Navy Ministry to Publish Booklet: 30th Anniversary of the Russo-Japanese War

(Tokyo) The Navy Ministry will publish 100,000 copies of a booklet entitled "The Achievements of the Battle of the Sea of Japan and the Issue of Naval Disarmament" on May 27th, the 30th anniversary of the Russo-Japanese War, and distribute them to various sectors. The content includes: 1. Introduction; 2. Complete Annihilation of the Russian First Pacific Squadron; 3. The Voyage of the Russian Second and Third Pacific Squadrons to the East, and the Battle of the Sea of Japan; 4. Lessons from the Battle of the Sea of Japan and the Issue of Naval Disarmament; 5. Conclusion. The conclusion expresses the determination of the naval authorities, stating that Japan can independently maintain peace in the Far East, and that the major powers should entrust Japan with handling Far Eastern affairs. (Third Day Japan United Press Electric)

Japanese Seiyukai Party Sends Delegation to China

International Commercial Telegrams

Reuters Special Commercial News on May 3rd

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today, due to the rise in the pound, the price fell by four and a half pence to one hundred and forty-three shillings and eleven and a half pence.

London Silver Market: Local speculators sold, but China and India bought at the same time, so the price of silver rose slightly today. Spot price is thirty-three pence three seven five, up one pence. The futures price is thirty-three pence five six two five, up one pence zero six two five. The market closed steadily.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was calm this morning. The position of the pound is quite stable. The opening price for the British-American exchange rate was four dollars and eight eighths, the same as yesterday's closing price for American-British. It rose by two five within the first hour to four dollars and eight eighths. It fell by one two five at noon. It fell again by one eight seven five at 1:00 PM. The price turned firm in the last hour, rising by two five to four dollars and eight eighths. Also, one US dollar is worth four shillings and one and five five five pence in British gold.

British-French: The opening price for the British-French exchange rate was seventy-three francs and thirty-nine, up three pounds. It rose again by three pounds in the first hour. It fell by four pounds at noon to seventy-three francs thirty-eight. It rose by two pounds at 2:00 PM to seventy-three francs forty.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: Today (May 3rd), the New York cotton market was firm, with prices showing a slight increase, sympathizing with the rise in the price of silver. There are rumors that the government will alleviate the current cotton deadlock by selling regular cotton and buying new cotton for forward delivery. The weather in the West is reportedly very cold, and it is said that it has been raining.

British Cotton: Today, the Liverpool cotton market rose slightly, also sympathizing with the American cotton price. At 1:00 PM, the price for July delivery was 6.45, four pounds higher than yesterday's close.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened without movement. Climate reports from all wheat-growing areas, except the Southwest, are still good.

British Wheat: Today, prices in the Liverpool wheat market were slightly lower. At 1:00 PM, the price for July delivery was five shillings and six and two five pence, one two five lower than yesterday's close.

Rubber

London: The market opened calmly today. It trended toward stagnation before noon. At noon, the traded price for July/September delivery was five pence six eight seven five, zero six two five lower than yesterday's close.

New York: Market prices fell slightly today because the automobile industry strike situation continues to cause concern. Rumors of a devaluation of Dutch currency also have a limiting effect on trading.

Metals

London: Today (May 3rd), in the London metals market, due to the rise in the price of silver, the first session futures traded at thirty-six and a half pence, seven five higher than yesterday's second session price.

Securities

New York: Although there was no new development this morning to cause optimism, the market opened quite firmly. The US Chamber of Commerce and President Roosevelt's new opinions on government policies are openly broken. Because of the labor dispute in the automobile industry, people generally expect stock prices to be affected and fall, but today's opening prices rose slightly. There was some trading. Oil stocks were still being bought. Silver stocks rose due to the high silver price. Silver faction congressmen unanimously demanded the immediate implementation of silver purchase procedures, so the market merchants were very excited. Lowe's movie stocks also had firm prices, rising more than one dollar in the first hour after opening. The New York stock market prices are listed below:

Regulations Regarding Land Tax Should Be Consistent with the Spirit of the Land Law

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance instructed the finance departments and bureaus of each province and city, as well as the agencies under its jurisdiction, that the Land Implementation Law has been promulgated. This law is an important regulation for organizing land, and the collection, exemption, and disposal of land tax are all related to finance. Although the date of implementation has yet to be determined, all regulations related to land tax to be drafted in the future must be consistent with the spirit of the Land Law and its implementing regulations, to avoid multiple changes after implementation in the future. (Third Day Special Telegram)

Lifting of Blockaded Zones, State-Run Salt Sales Agencies Not Abolished

It telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for instructions, and the reply was that this type of state-run sales method can accurately determine the population numbers and consumption quantities in various regions, which can serve as the basis for promoting a controlled economy, and can prevent the exploitation of merchants, without hindering tax revenue at all. The Ministry of Finance therefore instructed the Hunan, Anhui, Zhejiang, and Fujian Salt Transportation Commissioners to follow the original order. (Third Day Special Telegram)

Women Escape from Nanjing Relief Home

(Nanjing) Women in the relief home are not allowed to go out. The guards closed the door to stop them, but it was ineffective, and they all rushed out and went straight to the municipal government to petition, using abuse as an excuse. Each police station was reported and the judicial section used cars to detain more than ten people outside the municipal government, and found three people in the hotel, and they were also detained. Today, four people went back voluntarily, and more than twenty people are at large. The authorities have decided to punish those who petitioned, and the method is to fine them to do hard labor and send them to the Badou Mountain Beggar Team for strict supervision, and strictly arrest those who escaped. Jiangsu Cotton Industry Improvement Institute Sets Up Cotton Control Experiment Zone

(Zhenjiang) In order to maintain the improvement of cotton varieties in Jiangsu Province and concentrate on promotion efforts, the Jiangsu Cotton Industry Improvement Institute has set up a Cotton Control Experiment Zone: (1) The Dingwan two zones within the Dongtai Dafeng Reclamation Company are the Dongtai Reclamation Area Experiment Zone. (2) The Third Zone within the base property of Yancheng Nantong University is the Yanfu Reclamation Area Experiment Zone. (3) The Suyu Zone within the Nantong Dayou Jin Salt Reclamation Company is the Tong Ru Hai Reclamation Area Experiment Zone. It is also designated that the Jinzi American Cotton is planted in the East China and Yanfu Reclamation Area Experiment Zone, and the Tuozi American Cotton is planted in the Tong Ruy Sea Reclamation Area Experiment Zone. Those who plant other varieties without authorization will be banned and punished. The seeds are sold at low prices by the Improvement Institute. The Kapok seeds produced in the area are transported and sold by the Cotton Production and Sales Cooperative, or sold on behalf of the Improvement Institute. Farmers are not allowed to sell them out of the area without authorization, and flower shops, ginned households, and hawkers are not allowed to set up shops in the area to buy them. All promotion and guidance matters in the area are the responsibility of the personnel dispatched by the Improvement Institute, and industrial police are organized for protection. (Third Day Central News Agency Electric)

Recovering Bandit Areas: Measures for Food Relief to the People; Promulgated by the General Headquarters for Compliance by Eight Provinces

Hankou Correspondence: In order to maintain the food supply for the people in the counties recovered from banditry and to facilitate purchase and transportation, Chairman Chiang instructed the General Headquarters to formulate "Measures for Food Relief to the People in the Counties Recovered from Banditry." On the 2nd, the Chengdu Headquarters telegraphed the measures to the eight provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu for compliance. The telegram and measures are as follows:

Telegram: It has been found that the counties on the northern and southern borders of Sichuan Province have long been plagued by bandits, and their assets have been depleted. During this period between harvests, there is a constant concern about the lack of rice and grain. The border counties of Yunnan, Guizhou, Hunan, Hubei, Shaanxi, and Gansu are also mostly areas disturbed by bandits, and the fear of food shortages is likely unavoidable. Although local relief agencies can organize emergency relief efforts and provide some assistance, it is like a drop in the bucket and difficult to cover everyone. Therefore, the only important matter after the recovery of the counties and areas affected by bandits is the issue of food for the people. If regulations are not clearly defined and remedies are not properly planned, there will be no way to properly address the aftermath once rice and grain are lacking. Now, fourteen articles of the Measures for Food Relief to the People in the Counties Recovered from Banditry and sample forms have been formulated and are being issued via telegram. It is hoped that you will investigate, instruct your subordinates to comply with them conscientiously, and report on the implementation.

Measures: (1) The General Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government has specially formulated these measures in order to maintain the food supply for the people in the counties recovered from banditry and to facilitate purchase and transportation. (2) In any locality in a county recovered from banditry where there is a perceived food shortage, the county magistrate should investigate and determine the amount needed, and instruct the county chamber of commerce or charitable organizations and reputable merchants to prepare funds to purchase and transport supplies from neighboring provinces and counties for relief. (3) If the groups or merchants in counties severely affected by bandits are unable to prepare funds, the county magistrate may petition the provincial government to allocate funds from local public funds for use, and the funds will be returned from the proceeds of the sale. If there are no public funds available, the county magistrate is permitted to petition the provincial government to provide a loan, and the method of lending will be determined by the provincial government. (4) If the purchase and transportation of rice and grain are handled with public funds or funds allocated by the provincial government, the county government should select reliable personnel, and public groups should each appoint a representative to handle the matter jointly. (5) The county government of each county purchasing rice and grain should first submit a detailed report to the provincial government for approval, listing the disaster areas, the extent of the disaster, the current situation, the amount of rice and grain needed, the types and quantities of rice and grain to be purchased, the purchasing agencies, groups, or merchants, the names of the people responsible for purchasing, and the intended purchasing locations and transportation dates. (6) After the provincial government approves the rice and grain for food relief, a rice and grain transportation permit should be issued as proof, and all checkpoints along the route should be notified, and the military stationed along the route should be requested to allow passage without taxation and to provide effective protection. (7) The rice and grain transportation mentioned above should be delivered to the county within the specified time limit, and the transportation permit received must be submitted to the county government for forwarding to the provincial government for cancellation. (8) If the quantity of rice and grain transported by the transportation agency, group, or merchant does not match the quantity stated on the transportation permit, or if other goods or contraband are smuggled in an attempt to profit, the discovering agency may detain the excess rice and grain or smuggled items and report to their respective superiors, who will forward the report to the provincial government for handling. If there is intentional obstruction or extortion, the grain transportation agency, group, or merchant may report to the county government, which will forward the report to the provincial government for investigation. (9) When the grain arrives in the county, the purchasing agency or merchant should report the actual amount of rice and grain purchased, as well as the cost and freight charges, to the county government for verification and record. (10) The county government should immediately review and approve the selling price based on the above report, and designate the selling locations, notifying the public in advance. The selling price should not exceed the total cost and freight charges in principle, but if the purchase and transportation are funded by merchants, a net profit of 5% may be added to the cost. (11) If any grain transportation agency or merchant is found to be hoarding and raising prices or engaging in other fraudulent activities, the county government should investigate and report to the provincial government for punishment according to law. (12) These measures do not apply to areas that have not been affected by bandits. (13) These measures may be amended at any time by order if there are any omissions. (14) These measures will take effect from the date of promulgation (May 2nd).

Sichuan: Candidates for Commissioners of Various Districts

The entire Sichuan province is divided into eighteen administrative districts; the provincial government has submitted the names to the General Headquarters for appointment of commissioners.

Chongqing Correspondence: The decision by the Sichuan provincial government to establish administrative inspector commissioners has divided the entire province into eighteen districts. The candidates for commissioner for thirteen of these districts, excluding Wang Cifu, Shen Peng, and Luo Jingyou, who were transferred from the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, have all been carefully selected by the provincial government chairman Liu Xiang from various sources and submitted to Chairman Chiang for approval. The formal appointment by the General Headquarters will take place shortly. Each commissioner will assume their post after receiving the order. The candidates for the remaining five districts are currently being solicited and will be submitted for appointment soon. The following is a list of the appointed commissioners for the thirteen districts and their respective residences and jurisdictions:

District 1: Commissioner Li Weilun, currently the deputy director of the Second Division of the General Staff, residing in Xinjin, with jurisdiction over the twelve counties of Chengdu, Huayang, Xindu, Guanxian, Xinfan, Zhangxian, Wenjiang, Bianliu, Xinjin, Chongqing, Chongning, and Pengxian.

District 2: Commissioner Wang Cifu, formerly the commissioner of the Luoyang district of Henan, residing in Zizhong, with jurisdiction over the eight counties of Ziyang, Zizhong, Neijiang, Weixian, Rongxian, Jingyan, Renshou, and Jianyang.

District 3: Commissioner Shen Peng, formerly the commissioner of the Chuzhou district of Anhui, residing in Yongchuan, with jurisdiction over the ten counties of Baxian, Hongjin, Qijiang, Yongchuan, Rongchang, Dazu, Bishan, Jiangbei, Hechuan, and Tongliang.

District 4: Commissioner Liang Zhenglin, formerly a Daoyin (circuit intendant) and salt transport commissioner, residing in Meishan, with jurisdiction over the nine counties of Hongya, Jiajiang, Qingshen, Meishan, Danleng, Pengshan, Pujiang, Qionglai, and Dayi.

District 5: Commissioner Chen Bingguang, currently a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, residing in Mabian, with jurisdiction over the seven counties of Jianwei, Leshan, Pingshan, Emei, Mabian, Ebian, and Leibo.

District 6: Commissioner Leng Xunnan, formerly a division commander, residing in Yibin, with jurisdiction over the nine counties of Yibin, Nanxi, Changning, Qingfu, Jiang'an, Xingwen, Hongxian, Gaoxian, and Junyun.

District 7: Commissioner not yet determined, residing in Luxian, with jurisdiction over the eight counties of Luxian, Longchang, Fushun, Hejiang, Naxi, Gulin, and Xuyong.

District 8: Commissioner not yet determined, residing in Youyang, with jurisdiction over the eight counties of Fuling, Fengdu, Nanchuan, Pengshui, Qianjiang, Youyang, Xiushan, and Shizhu.
