Shanghai Municipal Anti-Epidemic Campaign

School Inoculations to Begin This Month; Disinfection of Drinking Water to Begin Next Month

The citywide anti-epidemic campaign in both the Chinese and foreign-controlled areas began simultaneously on May 1st. In the Chinese-controlled area, the campaign began with schools. The schools are divided into five groups. Those that have already been inoculated include Meixi, Minglun, Wuben Elementary School, Tangwan, Caotang, Shihua, Xicheng, Wanzhu, Navigation, Anlv, Songxue, and other schools, totaling 6,318 injections. The campaign will continue. Starting next week, another group will be added, and the distribution will be slightly changed to three groups in South Shanghai, two groups in Zhabei, and one group in the rural area. In the foreign-controlled area, school inoculations are also actively underway. Starting June 1st, disinfection of drinking water will begin. There are a total of twenty people in the disinfection team: eight in South Shanghai, eight in Zhabei, and four in Pudong and other areas. Stagnant ponds, pools, and well water will be disinfected by the team. The investigation has already started and is expected to be completed this month, after which the disinfection work will begin immediately.

First Special District Court Announcement: Strictly Investigate Racketeering and Swindling

The Jiangsu Shanghai First Special District Local Court announces the following: Shanghai is a place where people from all directions gather, and the good and bad are mixed. There are many racketeers and swindlers. When there are lawsuits, they often falsely claim to the parties involved that they have connections with certain officials or prosecutors of the court and can speak on their behalf, or they impersonate court personnel and offer to gather information. They use various excuses to seek money. If they are not successful, they will threaten and intimidate. The parties involved, due to lack of knowledge, are deceived, causing harm to the people's legal rights and the court's reputation, which is extremely regrettable. This court issued Announcement No. 1368 in January of the 22nd year, earnestly informing and reasoning about the situation. For the past two years, the atmosphere has gradually improved. However, we worry that complacency will arise over time. Therefore, we are issuing a new warning. You must know that this court handles cases impartially. Winning or losing a case depends on the evidence and the law. Detention and bail also have certain standards. They cannot be swayed by any influence or favor. If anyone claims that they can intercede with the court, they are intending to extort money. You should report them truthfully or secretly. We will investigate and prosecute them according to the law. This court will also send personnel to conduct secret investigations at any time. If anyone is found to be engaging in racketeering and swindling, they will be severely punished to serve as a warning and to protect the good people. Everyone should be aware of this. Sincerely, this announcement, May 3, 24th year of the Republic of China, President Guo Yunguan, Chief Prosecutor Xiang Zhejunn.

Postman Steals Stamps Case

Sentenced to Three Years in Prison

Dong Jianyuan, a Shandong native, 33 years old, residing at 271 Fulili Road, working as a postman, previously served in Harbin. After the Northeast was lost on September 18th, Dong entered the customs and served in post offices in Pingjin and other places. He was recently transferred to Shanghai and assigned as letter carrier No. 807 in the Central 18th District Post Office, specializing in collecting letters from mailboxes on various roads. He has been serving for five or six years, and his salary has increased to 53 yuan per month. However, Dong's expenses were too high, and he could not make ends meet. So, he had a whimsical idea. Recently, he has been hiding dozens of letters collected from mailboxes, tearing off the stamps, selling them for cash, and destroying the letters. This led to senders inquiring and questioning the post office because their letters were not delivered. The post office then sent investigators to conduct a secret investigation. On the afternoon of the 17th of last month, at 3:00 PM, when Dong was collecting letters from a mailbox at the Xujiahui Road Sacred Heart Bridge in the French Concession, he hid the letters by his side. He was spotted by an investigator, who immediately grabbed Dong and found 56 letters in his pocket. He was arrested and taken to the police station. Dong confessed to privately tearing off the stamps and destroying the letters. Investigators were also dispatched to his home, where they seized dozens of letters and sent them to the Second Special Court. The police department filed a public lawsuit against him for embezzlement and theft. The details have been reported previously. Li Changnian, a judge of the Second Special Court, concluded the preliminary hearing. Yesterday, Judge Li opened the court and ordered the defendant to be brought to the court. Dong Jianyuan was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for continuous embezzlement as a warning.

Haizhou Steamer Collides with Coffin Boat; Coffins Scatter and Drift

One Corpse is Missing; Crew Member Liu Qi Drowned

Jiangbei boatman Huang Youlan was entrusted by his fellow villagers to transport sixteen coffins back to their hometown for burial. On the afternoon of April 22nd, while sailing through the waters off Sheshan, his boat was suddenly rammed amidships by the Haizhou steamer of the Datong Company. The impact was so severe that Huang's boat was broken into two pieces. Everyone on board fell into the water. Except those who were rescued one after another. However, one crew member, Liu Qi (42 years old), was drowned. When he was retrieved, he was already dead. The sixteen coffins on board were scattered and drifted away. After a lot of searching by other boats, all the coffins were recovered. However, the lid of one coffin was lost, and the body was nowhere to be found. At that time, Huang Youlan simply coffined Liu Qi's body and transported it back to Shanghai. The body was temporarily placed at the Yangjiadu garbage pond in Pudong. Yesterday morning, Huang Youlan reported the situation to the local court and requested an autopsy. After receiving the report, the court dispatched Prosecutor Li Fen and Inspector Xuan Zhiming to Pudong to conduct an autopsy. When the judge arrived at the scene, Huang was not present. The judge ordered the local headman, Yang Zhenqing, to summon a worker to open the coffin. The headman went to find a worker, but due to the time, he could not find one. The judge then ordered the headman to transport the coffin to the Pujiang rescue station on the south pier on the next day (today) for an autopsy. After the judge finished his instructions, he returned to the court.

Suzhou Woman Chen Fengling Sues Zhu Duanfu for Abandonment

Requests 20,000 Yuan for Living Expenses and Recovers 1,000 Yuan in Private Savings

Chen Fengling, a 27-year-old woman from Suzhou residing at 8 Peace Lane, Aiwunyi Road, recently retained lawyers such as Zhang Yijun to file a lawsuit with the Civil Court of the First Special Court against Zhu Duanfu (also known as Zhu Chunqiu), residing at 94 Wuding Road, for malicious abandonment. She is requesting 20,000 yuan in alimony and the return of 1,000 yuan in private savings. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Luo Chongtai came to the Civil Court No. 7 to summon the plaintiff and defendant. Neither party appeared in court, and each retained lawyers to represent them. The plaintiff's agent, Lawyer Zhang, stated that Chen Fengling is currently 27 years old. When she was 17 years old, she met Zhu Duanfu

and began living together.

At that time, the defendant claimed that he was still unmarried. Therefore, they were known as husband and wife both internally and externally. However, after living together, she discovered that the defendant was already married. Because what was done could not be undone, she could only reluctantly become a concubine. For ten years, their relationship was harmonious. Unexpectedly, in July of last year, the defendant met a dancer. As a result, his attitude suddenly changed. First, he used the excuse of investing in stocks to swindle 1,000 yuan from the plaintiff's private savings. Then, their love broke down, and he abandoned her without care. Although the plaintiff and the defendant are not husband and wife, she has been

a concubine.

For ten years now, this spring, he abandoned her because she was older and less attractive. Not only is this unforgivable, but it is also illegal. Furthermore, the plaintiff is weak and ill and has no ability to produce. Her future life will be in a state of desperation. Therefore, she has no choice but to request that the court order the defendant to pay the plaintiff a one-time alimony payment of 20,000 yuan. The defendant inherited his grandfather's estate. In the Chadaijiao area, he owns a lot of land. When the plaintiff and defendant were living together, the defendant gave the plaintiff

200 yuan per month

In addition, he gave her 300 yuan on festivals. Therefore, the plaintiff is now requesting 20,000 yuan for living expenses. The calculation method is to deposit 20,000 yuan in the bank. If she gets one percent interest, she can get 200 yuan per month, which can maintain her life. All of the private savings of 1,000 yuan should be ordered to be returned. The defendant should also bear the litigation costs. Then, the defendant's lawyer, Lu Dingming, argued that the plaintiff used to be a prostitute. In 1926, she was listed at Xiaohuayuan, named Hua Baoyu Laoqi. Later, she was transferred to Fuyuli

Rowland Bookstore.

At that time, because the defendant was still young, he inevitably frequented brothels. He met the plaintiff at that time. At that time, the plaintiff had a patron named Chen, who had the intention of keeping her as a mistress. However, it did not materialize. Because the plaintiff's business was poor, she invited the defendant to help, who frequently spent money on wine and entertainment. In January 1928, the two parties were deeply in love. The plaintiff stopped engaging and rented a house with her stepmother. The defendant went there often and gave her living expenses of 100 yuan, or several tens of yuan, or one hundred and several tens of yuan, depending on his economic ability. There was no such thing as a monthly payment of 200 yuan. Last year, due to the economic downturn, the defendant

was also affected.

His economy was tight. Therefore, he asked the plaintiff to move into his home. Because the plaintiff had other hobbies, he repeatedly advised her to stop. The plaintiff not only refused, but also used vulgar language. As a result, their love broke down, and the defendant stopped going there. This is just a friendship relationship. There is no legal basis. There is no obligation to support her. Therefore, he cannot afford even one yuan. As for the private savings of 1,000 yuan, the plaintiff should be asked to provide evidence. Judge Luo ruled that the case was clear. After the arguments of both lawyers were concluded, he announced that the verdict would be announced at 9:00 AM on the 8th of this month.

American Palmer Sues Chinese for Embezzlement

Claims Income from Pier Was Appropriated; Court Sends Accountant to Audit Books

American Palmer, manager of the Shishi Foreign Firm at 176 West Shanxi Road, retained Lawyer Lin Luanqing to file a criminal complaint with the First Special District Court against Guangdong natives Chen Wenxiang, Chen Huanzhi, and Cheng Jingchi for business embezzlement, fraudulent financial gain, and breach of trust. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang opened the court for a hearing. The facts are as follows: The plaintiff purchased the Tongtai Pier in Pudong from Dachang Bank in December of the previous year for 75,000 yuan. On June 4th of the following year, he appointed the first defendant, Chen Wenxiang, as the pier manager, Ren Wangzhong as the business manager, and the Xinji Construction Factory was responsible for constructing the necessary buildings and equipment on the pier. Contracts were signed. On October 2nd of the 23rd year, ships began to dock at the pier, and business began. However, the first defendant colluded with his staff, namely the third defendant, Cheng Jingchi, to completely misappropriate all income from the pier. They never reported the income and expense accounts to the plaintiff or the business manager. Wang Zhong privately appointed Chen Tiwu and Jin Youmei as pier brokers, collecting a guarantee deposit of 12,000 yuan. He further appointed Li Haiqing as the gang leader, collecting a guarantee deposit of 5,000 yuan. All of this was pocketed privately, causing the plaintiff's pier office in the Mainland Building on Jiujiang Road to close due to lack of funds. The first defendant is undoubtedly guilty of business embezzlement under Article 357 of the Criminal Code. The second defendant did not personally manage affairs and most often let the third defendant handle everything. Receiving and spending money was the third defendant's important task. The third defendant and the first defendant are suspected of colluding to commit embezzlement, which is also unavoidable. The first defendant falsely established the Yixing store and entered into a gang contract. He further colluded with his father, the second defendant, Chen Huanzhi, using the name of the Fuan Hardware Store to issue bills and pay one bill twice, thereby defrauding money. The first defendant also used receipts from Gu Xinji Construction Factory that were not yet due to deceive the business manager, Wang Zhong, into paying out money for his private use. The crimes under Articles 363 and 1366 of the same law are also obvious. The defendants, knowing they are guilty, have been avoiding capture and have no fixed whereabouts, except for occasional visits to the pier to collect money. They may be planning to flee. In court, each defendant denied the charges when asked. Due to the complexity of the case, an accountant was appointed to audit the books. The hearing was adjourned to a later date.

City Government Plans to Open Yu Garden; Cui Xiu Tang to Open Automatically

Vendors Along the Garden to be Banned; Qianye and Tangye Decide After Meetings

The city government's plan to open the Yiyuan Garden in the Yemiao was passed at the last municipal administration meeting. Subsequently, the Social Affairs Bureau convened three groups: the Doumi Qianye and Tangye, to discuss the opening measures. Now, the Cui Xiu Tang of the rice industry will open automatically. The Qianye and Tangye are scheduled to hold meetings today and tomorrow to decide. The city government will also ban vendors along the garden to improve appearances. The following is a report from the Dagongshe reporter on the various situations:

Banning Vendors to Improve Appearances

The Yilang Yiyuan has always been a famous scenic spot in the city. It originally belonged to the public. The scenery is quiet, and the greenery is lush. The rockeries in the garden are winding and exquisite. Every spring and autumn, birds sing and flowers are fragrant, adding to the pleasant atmosphere. Later, due to indemnity relations, the entire garden was leased to the Qianye Guild, the Doumi Industry's Cui Xiu Tang, and the Tangye's Dianchun Tang, which were divided to establish meeting places with high walls in between. Since then, this scenic area has been unable to be seen. The city government now plans to open the garden for Chinese and foreign people to enjoy. However, the vendors around the garden are cluttered, which hinders the appearance. Therefore, before opening the garden, it has been decided to ban vendors along the route. The banning measures are being discussed by the Social Affairs Bureau.

Cui Xiu Tang to Open Automatically

The Doumi Industry Association's Cui Xiu Tang occupies three-fifths of the Yiyuan and is separated by another wall. Thousands of days are needed each year for the repairs to the houses and rockeries, which are funded by the association. After the city government advocated opening the park, it has been decided through meetings to open it automatically. Visitors will be charged a small fee to pay for repairs. At the same time, the number of visitors per day will be limited to only 300 to 400 people. It is expected to open after the arrangements are completed.

Inner Garden and Dianchun to be Decided at Meetings

At the previous meeting convened by the Social Affairs Bureau, the Inner Garden of the Qianye Guild and the Dianchun Tang of the Tangye Trade Association stated that the matter concerned the property of the groups and that they would need to hold separate meetings to decide. It is now known that the guild has scheduled a general membership meeting today to decide whether or not to open it.

The Ningbo Sojourners Association in Shanghai will convene a general meeting of members on the 19th of this month to report on the association's affairs over the past year and propose events. It is also heard that the term of office for the association's executive supervisory fund committee expires this year. Apart from retaining one-third of the members in accordance with the regulations, the election for the new members is scheduled for the 22nd and 23rd of this month. The association has reported to the Municipal Party Department and the Bureau of Social Affairs, requesting them to send personnel to supervise the event in order to ensure due diligence.

Catholic Pilgrims Visit Our Lady of Sheshan

Every year in May according to the Gregorian calendar is the Holy Mother's Month for Catholics. Traditionally, the Catholic Action of Shanghai organizes a pilgrimage to Our Lady of Sheshan, which both male and female, young and old Catholics can join, which is a grand event. Now that the Holy Mother's Month is approaching again, Mr. Lu Bohong, the president of the association, has contacted the Railway Bureau to arrange special trains, which will depart from the South Railway Station at exactly 4:00 AM on May 5th. After arriving at Yaojinggang, they will transfer to tugboats to reach Sheshan directly. Priests will solemnly conduct Mass. After the service, they will return by the same route and arrive back in Shanghai at approximately 7:00 PM in the afternoon. The fare is one yuan per person. When boarding the train, station staff will check tickets. The association will send several staff members along the way to take care of everything. Those who are interested in participating in the pilgrimage and receiving divine grace can go to the Catholic Action Office in Dongjiadu, Nanshi, to pre-purchase pilgrimage tickets. It is reported that ticket sales have been very active recently, with limited tickets remaining. Purchases are encouraged as soon as possible since no temporary tickets will be available at the station.

Zhu Xuefan's Speech on Labor Day (Continued)

According to central statistical reports, 80% of the national population are illiterate, and the labor community accounts for the majority of the illiterate. To take the recent statistics from a survey of Jiangwan as an example, Jiangwan has a total population of 13,764 people, of which 11,657 are illiterate and only 2,107 are literate. This is a reliable figure. Within this illiterate population, what is the level of knowledge of our farmers and workers? How low is the standard of mass education in China? In today's increasingly serious international situation and the declining national status, how can we talk about saving the country with an illiterate and unknowledgeable populace who do not understand the world situation and the crisis of the nation-state, and who lack a grand vision of the nation-state? If we do not start with transforming them through knowledge and education, then we will fall into empty talk and mere slogans, only able to follow others in shouting slogans. Therefore, the municipal government, the municipal party department, and leaders from all walks of life have seen this and initiated the literacy movement. The first step in the plan is to start with literacy, eliminating illiteracy, especially among the workers who make up the largest illiterate population in the city. Liang Rengong said, "What is education? Education is teaching people how to be human beings, teaching people to be modern people." This means that everyone must be a modern person. In primitive times, when social culture had not been established, everything was barbaric and unreasonable. At that time, not being educated, not reading, and not being literate were not a big deal. But now is not that kind of era anymore. Now is the age of wisdom; the foolish and unknowledgeable will be eliminated and will not be able to survive. Dewey once said, "Education is essential for life. Without education, human life will stop." This means that people who are not educated not only cannot live themselves, but also affect and harm the entire society. Therefore, literacy, continuing education, and receiving education are indeed extremely important, especially in today's China, when saving the country and the nation brook no delay. Can we still be illiterate and unknowledgeable? The Analects say, "If a craftsman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools." If we want to revitalize the nation and rejuvenate the country, we must first become literate. Literacy leads to knowledge, knowledge leads to thought, and thought leads to the determination to revitalize the nation. Then we will definitely be able to make the nation-state prosperous and strong. Today is the first day of the Shanghai Literacy Movement Week. I would like to offer three points to the workers of the city and the workers of the country. First, labor literacy. I have already mentioned the importance of labor's status in society and its close relationship with the country. Therefore, labor literacy is certainly the most important task at present. So I hope people in the labor community and people from all walks of life will recognize the importance of labor and support labor literacy. All our fellow workers in Shanghai and the country must also recognize the benefits of literacy. If we want good treatment, improve our lives, raise the status of workers, revitalize the nation, and strengthen the country, we must strive for literacy. Second, labor service. The level of knowledge of Chinese workers is so low that they do not even recognize a single character. How can we achieve the goal of universal literacy? This requires following the labor service methods and spirit of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Those who teach literacy must of course work hard, and those who receive literacy education should study diligently and tirelessly. Many young people say that we work all day long and have no time to study. Those who are older also say that they are too old to study. On the surface, this seems to make sense, but in reality, it is just laziness and complacency. We know that the world is evolving, and each era is different. Even if we cannot run ahead of the times, we should at least keep up with the times. Now is an era of extraordinary struggle. If we do not work hard, we will be eliminated. If we do not work hard, we will not be able to survive. If we spend a little more time to become literate and read, it will not only be of great benefit to the individual, but also benefit the country and society. Therefore, the spirit of labor service is a great force in promoting social progress. Third, labor-capital cooperation. China is now a foolish, poor, and backward country. To make progress, we must first solve poverty. To solve poverty, we must also solve foolishness. In the golden age of the worker movement in 1927, the aim was to attack capitalists and shout slogans to overthrow them. But are there any capitalists in China now? There are not enough to even qualify as capitalists. Many of China's past small capitalists have now been overwhelmed by the imported capitalists of imperialism. China has almost no capitalists, so there is naturally no question of overthrowing them. In order to increase production and revitalize the nation, we must actively implement labor-capital cooperation. In the current situation, if labor and capital do not cooperate, both sides will suffer under the high pressure of imperialism and perish together. We need a comprehensive solution for China. Internally, in terms of production, labor and capital should coordinate and develop national capital. Externally, we should use national capital to resist imperialist capital. Fellow workers of Shanghai, we must break free from our restraints, create an environment, and escape from the dark hell. We must rely on our own strength. If everyone can run forward together, I think China will definitely have a way out. Today is International Labor Day and the first day of the Shanghai Literacy Movement Promotion Week, so I have talked about the past process of the labor movement, the importance of literacy, and the efforts that workers should make today. I hope that everyone can work hard to make 80% of the illiterate literate, thoughtful, capable of struggling, and willing to sacrifice, so that they can save themselves, save society, save the country, and save the nation.

Huang Yuqi Submits a Petition to the Ministry of Railways Requesting the Restoration of Dining Cars on the Ningbo-Cao'e Railway Line

Mr. Huang Yuqi of the financial community in this city is a native of Yuyao, Zhejiang, and is known for his public spirit and concern for society, especially his enthusiasm for his hometown. During his recent trip back to his hometown, Mr. Huang witnessed the hardships of travelers and the embarrassment of merchants on the Ningbo-Cao'e Railway line. Everyone felt that the cancellation of dining cars and the reduction of attendants on the line last year caused great inconvenience to passengers, making it difficult to obtain food and drink and difficult to transport luggage. Those who were helping the elderly and carrying children all had a sense of being lost and helpless. After arriving in his hometown, Mr. Huang also heard comments that the line urgently needed reform and rectification. Therefore, after returning to Shanghai, Mr. Huang, in order to facilitate merchants and travelers, telegraphed the Ministry of Railways and submitted a petition to the two Railway Bureaus, requesting that dining cars be restored and attendants be hired on the Ningbo-Cao'e Railway line as soon as possible. The telegram to the Ministry of Railways reads: (Omitted above) The Ningbo-Cao'e Railway line is an important transportation route for Ningbo and Shaoxing, and a necessary route for gentry and merchants. In the past, there were dining cars to provide meals for passengers and attendants to serve travelers, which was convenient for merchants and made them feel at home when traveling. The level of service was equivalent to that on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways. Unexpectedly, at the end of last year, the line suddenly cancelled dining cars and reduced the number of attendants to only one, which caused great inconvenience to passengers. Not only was there a lack of meals, but even tea and snacks were also difficult to obtain. Travelers from the countryside had to rush to the station from dozens of miles away, and they were bound to be hungry. It was difficult to endure several hours of hunger in the train. If there were restaurants outside the station, they could eat in advance while waiting for the train, but there are no such shops outside the station, which makes people feel hungry. In the past, there were many attendants on the train to serve passengers and perform the duties of cleaning the train. Since the cancellation, only one person has been left. No one can help passengers carry their luggage. The strong can carry it themselves, but the elderly and passengers carrying children cannot bear the heavy burden and are unable to take care of themselves. They are lost and helpless, and their hardships are even greater. As for hygiene, the trains lack cleaning and are difficult to keep clean. Summer has arrived, which is of great concern to hygiene. Even if the attendant is diligent, it is difficult to provide comprehensive service. In short, all of these issues are of vital concern to passengers. Therefore, dining cars and attendants must not be cancelled. Merchants and travelers seek comfort and convenience during their travels, and they are willing to spend a little more money for this. Therefore, I am submitting this telegram to your department, requesting the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau to restore dining cars and hire more attendants on the Ningbo-Cao'e Railway line in order to facilitate merchants and benefit travelers. (Omitted below) The petition to the two Railway Bureaus is the same.

Wang Xinggao Appeals for an Investigative Hearing

Wang Xinggao, a native of Funing and the main culprit in the assassination of Dian Jiapeng, the former manager of the Great World Amusement Park, escaped at the time and remained at large. It was not until the end of last year that the French Concession Police, based on a tip from Zhao Guangfu, who had been apprehended, arrested Wang in Room 513 of the Central Hotel on the evening of December 13. He was sent to the Special Second Court and prosecuted for premeditated murder. After the trial, Wang was sentenced to life imprisonment and deprivation of political rights for life. The defendant was dissatisfied with the verdict and filed an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. These details have been reported in the newspapers. At 10:30 AM yesterday, Judge Yue of the High Court's Third Branch opened an investigative hearing and brought Wang to the court for interrogation. According to Wang's statement, he still denied involvement in the murder, repeatedly claiming injustice. He also stated that he was a civil servant and had many enemies. Moreover, at the time of the incident, he was serving in prison in Wuchang, and he did not know Dian Jiapeng, so why would he kill him? He also did not know Zhou Xiaomujiang and others. He only went by the name Wang Xinggao and did not have a second name of Wang Jinkui. He requested an investigation. After the court verified the statement, it ordered Wang to submit his reasons for appeal as soon as possible and wait for a scheduled retrial. After the discussion, Wang was ordered to be returned to the detention center to await further instructions.

No Bids for Shun'an Steamer; Creditors Jointly Agree to Maintain

The Shun'an steamer of the Shun'an Company was involved in a lawsuit due to the incident in which the shipowner Ouyang Tai attempted to blow it up, but later had a change of heart and did not carry out the attack. Details of the incident have been reported in the previous news. It is now learned that the company has been severely affected by this incident, and the ship has been detained and docked in the Longhua Pudong. The creditors have successively hired lawyers such as Lin Luanqing and Gan Lin to sue the local court for repayment of debts and requested that the ship be sold to offset the debts. Creditors such as China United Assurance Company are suing for 20,122 yuan in foreign currency, Jiangnan Shipbuilding Plant for 6,500 yuan, Kang Zhenkui for 1,025 yuan and 35 yuan, Hengli Bank for 6,000 yuan, Yitai Coal Company for 1,400 yuan, Yichang Hardware Company for 3,277 yuan, and Jia Hua Bank for 1,000 yuan. After investigation and judgment, the Shun'an steamer was put up for auction, but no one made an offer. This is now the third auction, and the minimum price is 40,896 yuan. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhu Yinqiao of the Enforcement Court opened the hearing. Lawyers Lin Luanqing and Gan Lin appeared in court and stated that if the ship remains unsold for a long time, they are deeply concerned that further delays will cause damage to the ship's machinery. They urged that a solution be found as soon as possible. After verifying the statements, the judge instructed all creditors to discuss joint maintenance measures to avoid losing their principal. Lawyers Lin and others replied that they would consult and report back later.

Cigarette Smuggling Suppression Association: Cigarette Paper Public Warehouse Established

Dagong News reports that the Cigarette Smuggling Suppression Association, organized by the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance and the Shanghai Cigarette Association, has established a public warehouse to store cigarette paper required by the city and strictly prevent tax evasion due to the prevalence of tax-evading cigarette paper in Shanghai. It is learned that the cigarette public warehouse, which has been prepared for many years by the Tax Bureau, has been established. The warehouse is located in Tilanqiao, with four floors and adjacent to the Huangpu River, making loading and unloading extremely convenient. The Tax Bureau stipulates that all cigarette paper purchased by merchants in the city must be stored in the public warehouse. The warehouse rent is very cheap, about 20-30% lower than ordinary warehouses.

Due to the current sluggish business conditions, the British-owned Shanghai Gas Company laid off three lamplighters from the street lighting department, Yang A'er, Zhou Zhangfu, etc., yesterday. In accordance with the regulations, the laid-off workers were paid severance pay. Yang A'er received 297.08 yuan, Zhou Zhangfu received 313.30 yuan, and He Xiangyou received 363.10 yuan. Standard Milk Sales are Booming

Endorsed by Dr. Wu Liande and Many Renowned Doctors

Standard Milk is a product of China Standard Milk Bean Milk Company. The company was established by Shanghai Chinese and Western gentry and merchants, including Xu Xinliu, Liu Hongsheng, Ding Wenjiang, Wang Zimin, Tang Shoumin, Wu Yun Chu, Lamb, Bode, and Xue Shi, with a share capital of over 200,000 yuan. Its main products are Standard Milk, Bean Milk Substitute Powder, and Frozen Custard. Standard Milk is a scientifically modified milk that is very similar in nature to human milk and is currently popular in Europe and the United States. It is especially popular in Southeast Asia. Bean Milk Substitute Powder is the latest invention of scientists, rich in nutrition and convenient to take. The selling price is only about 20% of ordinary milk substitutes. Frozen Custard is only made by the American Hai Ning Foreign Company in Shanghai for many years. Since the "Beauty Brand" is in short supply, the company specially produces "White Rose Brand" frozen custard to meet the needs of the community. Currently, Standard Milk has already begun operations, and Bean Milk Substitute Powder and White Rose Brand Frozen Custard will also be launched this month. The company guarantees that the milk fat content in Standard Milk will be 4.5% in all bottles throughout the year. The vitamin content is also very high. It has obtained a special license from the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement. The Municipal Council manages it by citing the A-grade milk regulations. Since its launch just a month ago, daily sales have reached more than 1,000 pounds. In the beginning, most consumers were foreigners. Since the endorsement of famous doctors in Shanghai and the publication of promotional comments by Dr. Wu Liande after personally visiting the factory, it has gradually been trusted by the ladies of Shanghai. In particular, after the company announced the characteristics of Standard Milk and its modification details in newspapers, it gained the confidence of the intellectual class. Recently, more than one hundred new households have been added every day, and the company is struggling to keep up with demand. The previous doubts about freshness and rumors about the lack of milk fat have been dispelled. According to the person in charge of the company, the reason for achieving unexpected success in such a short period of time is not only thanks to the promotion efforts of the medical community, but also to the social circles appreciation for quality goods. The superiority of Standard Milk lies not only in its quality exceeding the Municipal Council's A-grade milk regulations, but also in its particularly fair selling price. A half-pound small bottle is sold for only 15 cents, a one-pound medium bottle for 28 cents, and a two-pound large bottle for 50 cents. The company's business location is at No. 60, Nanxun Road, telephone number 40080. You can place orders by phone or mail at any time from 7:00 AM to 10:00 PM every day.

Xue Mingjian Petitions the Construction Department to Promote Rabbit Farming

The Department Orders the Wuxi Extension Office to Conduct a Pilot Program

Xin Xin News reports that Xue Mingjian, a member of the business community, submitted a petition to the Construction Department the day before yesterday to promote rabbit farming. The original petition stated: "The petition is to request that the agricultural extension offices in all counties be ordered to promote rabbit farming to relieve the rural economy. The rural economy of Jiangsu Province has traditionally relied on silk as a major source of income. Since the failure of mulberry cultivation, the rural economy has frequently gone bankrupt. Without a replacement, it will be difficult to recover. It is believed that rabbit farming is the most suitable for rural breeding in our country. Japan has promoted it throughout the country for the past five or six years. The benefits obtained have surpassed chicken and bee farming, and will be on par with silk. I implore you to order the Wuxi Agricultural Extension Office to allocate special funds to cultivate rabbit breeds or to set up a rabbit breeding farm, stipulating that it will be popularized throughout the county within two years in order to recover the 24 million yuan loss from silk farming. Then extend it to the other sixty counties in the province, so that farmers throughout the province can maintain their livelihoods. Attached is an article of sixty-five pages on how to recover from the failure of silk farming in Wuxi, which shows a glimpse. Separately, the humble compilation "Practical Rabbit Farming Method" will be sent separately after printing is completed. I implore you to quickly allocate special funds and implement promotion for the benefit of the rural area." Yesterday, the Construction Department's response was received, stating that the proposal to promote rabbit farming to relieve the rural economy is insightful. The provincial silk trial farm should be ordered to conduct a pilot program at the original site of the Wuxi County Extension Office. It can be promoted after the success is achieved. This is the reply.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Shandong and its surrounding areas are cloudy, turning overcast, with rain. The wind direction is uncertain, due to a low-pressure area in Henan. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy, but still clear and fine, with localized fog and gentle southeast to southwest winds. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait are overcast, with strong northeasterly breezes. A small hurricane northwest-west of Yap Island appears to be still moving northwest-west. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 72.1 degrees and the lowest was 49.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 62.2 degrees and the lowest was 54.9 degrees.

Shanghai City's Special Publication for the Illiteracy Eradication Education Promotion Week

Announcement to Citizens

— Wu Tiecheng

Dear Compatriots:

You probably all know the pain of being illiterate. An illiterate person cannot keep accounts, write letters, read newspapers, understand posters on the walls, understand official notices, or understand world affairs. Sometimes, it is simply having eyes but being blind, becoming a "bright-eyed blind person." Their suffering is truly indescribable.

In our China, about eighty out of every hundred people are illiterate. Shanghai also has hundreds of thousands of illiterate people. To relieve the suffering of the people and revitalize our nation, we must first make all these illiterate people literate. To this end, we will begin a large-scale literacy education movement starting from July 1st of this year. We plan to give hundreds of thousands of illiterate men, women, old and young in Shanghai the opportunity to become literate within one year, and also provide them with some general knowledge, guidance, and civic training, so that they all become healthy citizens.

The methods we will use are: First, divide Shanghai into twenty-two districts, with sixty literacy classes established in each district, for a total of one thousand three hundred and twenty literacy classes in the city. We will compel illiterate people to attend classes for one hour a day. Not only will there be no tuition fees, but we will also provide books. They can graduate after studying for two months. Second, for those who really cannot go to school every day, we will send teachers to their homes to provide individual guidance. After two months, if they pass our exams, we can also give them graduation certificates. By that time, they will be able to keep accounts, write letters, and read simple newspapers. Not only will it be convenient for themselves, but all of us in Shanghai will feel very proud. If someone does not cherish themselves and does not want to become literate, then we will definitely give them appropriate punishment.

However, without an investigation, our methods cannot be implemented. Because we do not yet know who is illiterate, how many illiterate people there are, who can attend school in the morning, who can attend school in the evening, and who really cannot attend school. How can we run schools and send teachers? Therefore, the Jiangwan Experimental District has been dispatching a large number of investigators since April 10th, the Nanshi Experimental District has been doing so since May 1st, and the other twenty districts will be doing so from May 10th, carrying identification documents to conduct on-the-ground investigations of illiterate people and also persuade them to go to school.

As mentioned above, this literacy education movement is clearly a very heavy and difficult task. We have few people and limited ability, so we cannot help but hope that all sectors of society will provide more support. China is fortunate!

Literacy Education All-Out Mobilization

— Pan Gongzhan

Citizens of the Republic of China, our compatriots, more than 70 percent are illiterate, meaning that more than 300 million citizens are illiterate. Even though the citizens of Shanghai are more enlightened than those in the interior, I am afraid that the total number of illiterate people, young and old, including those in the concessions, will reach about 1.5 million. In modern civilized countries, literate citizens account for at least 70 percent of the total population, and in many cases, they can reach more than 90 percent. Our country pales in comparison, and no wonder the national situation has declined to this point! Now, the slogan of "national rejuvenation" is filling the country, but if we do not start with universal education—literacy is the first step in universal education—everything will be empty talk. Therefore, the central government has stipulated seven movements, with the literacy movement ranking first.

The importance of universal literacy education need not be belabored. Now that the work of literacy education in Shanghai has begun, I dare to express my sincere hope to all citizens of Shanghai in twelve thousandths of a sincerity: "Literacy Education All-Out Mobilization." The so-called "mobilization" means that from the commander-in-chief, commanders of all routes, staff officers, brigade commanders, battalion commanders, and down to platoon leaders and brothers, all go to the front line to prepare for a desperate battle. The people in the rear, those who work, those who transport, those who provide medical assistance, also do their best to support the war. Only then is "all-out mobilization" worthy of the name. We must also unite the full power of the government and the people in the work of literacy education to fight a desperate battle against the phenomenon of "illiteracy" and a desperate battle against the root of "ignorance." Only with determination and unwavering resolve can we have hope of success.

Therefore, the work during the literacy education propaganda period is equivalent to the propaganda work during the period when the United States joined the European War seventeen or eighteen years ago, and also equivalent to the propaganda work during the period when Japan fought against Russia thirty years ago, and even more equivalent to the propaganda work of training people for air defense and self-defense in various countries around the world now. We must take the city's education sector as the main force, the city's industrial and commercial sectors as a joint army fighting together, and the city's party members and civil servants as the driving force, mobilizing all citizens who have received education and are capable of teaching others to read, to serve for literacy education under the command of the Literacy Education Committee and in accordance with all the regulations promulgated. Assuming that the literacy schools run by the municipal government are the frontal army, then the literacy schools run by individual citizens or groups are no different from the left and right wings of the army, and all other service groups, mutual aid groups, work-study groups, cultural cells, little teachers, etc., are no different from commando teams that are ever-changing and capable of winning by surprise. All of us who have received education, regardless of the level of education or the depth of knowledge, should clearly recognize that if there are still illiterate people in the city after one or two years, it is our shame and our failure. At the same time, we should work diligently and practically, build strongholds, and fight to the death, and we must achieve the goal of eliminating all illiteracy in the city. If citizens who are capable of teaching others to read, regardless of party, government, academia, industry, commerce, freelancers, or even entertainers and rural scholars, can truly mobilize as a whole and launch a general attack on the phenomena of "illiteracy" and "ignorance," I believe that the approximately 1.5 million illiterate people in the city will be transformed into literate citizens in the shortest possible time. I hope that knowledgeable citizens and citizens who can teach others to read will join the "literacy education army" and mobilize to the front line!

Eradicating Illiteracy

— Wu Kaixian

Eradicating illiteracy is a prerequisite for nation-building in every modern country. Whether it is the Soviet Union or Turkey, before the revolution, the literacy rate and the cultural level of their citizens were very low. After the revolution, their governments and people used all their strength to eradicate illiteracy. The current Soviet Union and Turkey have not only been transformed in various aspects such as politics and economy, but the general cultural level of the citizens has also improved, making it impossible to compare with before the revolution.

The improvement of a country's national cultural level cannot be said to be 100% based on the literacy level of the people, but it can be said that 90% of it is improved along with the improvement of literacy level. Writing is originally a master key to the treasure house of culture. Eradicating illiteracy allows all citizens to recognize and apply basic writing. The dissemination of culture naturally becomes easier, and the general cultural level of the citizens naturally improves.

There are no accurate statistics on the number of illiterate people in China. According to general estimates, it is about 80% or more. These 80% or more of people are not only unable to write letters, keep accounts, read newspapers, read posters, or read announcements, but also lack the necessary common knowledge about nature, society, the country, and the nation. The low level of national culture is simply impossible to find a second example of in modern civilized countries. This is truly a "national shame" of the first order. Everyone thinks about it. Such a country is really "not qualified." How can it survive in the current world? Therefore, if we want to revitalize the nation, build the country, and create culture, the first step must be to vigorously promote literacy education and eradicate illiteracy.

Shanghai is China's first major city, and also one of the world's top six cities. The cultural level of the general public is naturally higher than in other places. However, according to surveys and statistics, even in the urban area alone, excluding out-of-school children, there are still five to six hundred thousand illiterate citizens. Now that we are implementing literacy education, we must follow the planned plan and turn these five to six hundred thousand illiterate people into citizens who can recognize and apply basic writing within one year. This will set off a trend across the country, eradicate illiteracy, raise the cultural level, and wash away this rare "national shame." Only in this way can we talk about revitalizing the nation, building the country, and creating culture! Only in this way can we survive in the current world!

What is the Purpose of Literacy Education?

— Wu Xingya

The Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee has this time set down very detailed methods and made the greatest determination to promote literacy education, hoping to eliminate illiteracy within the urban area of Shanghai within one year.

After the illiteracy in Shanghai is eliminated, will the so-called blind people with open eyes see the light again, and will this be considered that the purpose of literacy education has been achieved? No, absolutely not. If illiterate people can all become literate, can keep track of their petty expenses, can write their own names, can read advertisements in newspapers, and can understand announcements from government offices, will this be considered that the purpose of literacy education has been achieved? This not only belittles the greatness of the literacy education movement, but also desecrates the dignity of the literacy education movement.

Originally, literacy education is by no means simply teaching people to read. In addition to literacy, there are two more important tasks: general knowledge guidance and civic training. Therefore, general knowledge guidance and civic training are the purpose of literacy education. Recognizing writing is just a method to achieve this purpose.

Of course, without first becoming literate, the two tasks of general knowledge guidance and civic training cannot be implemented. Therefore, the order of the literacy education movement is that writing education comes first, and general knowledge guidance and civic training come later. However, this distinction between before and after is by no means a distinction between importance. I believe that the strength and time required for general knowledge guidance and civic training should be greater and longer than that required for writing education in order to complete the mission of the literacy education movement.

As for how to guide general knowledge and how to train citizens, this matter is of great importance and requires careful thought. Of course, the Literacy Education Committee must unite educators, writers, and the publishing industry to work hard on this. Today (April 19th), I read a piece of news in the newspaper that can be provided to us as a reference for engaging in literacy education.

This piece of news is an electrical report from Berlin on April 28th, reporting that Germany will announce a citizenship law this year. Its Minister of the Interior said to people: Only those who serve the people and the country and prove their ability can obtain the honor of citizenship. Only citizens can be subject to public office, join the army, and have the right to vote. All those who receive citizenship must swear allegiance to the country and the head of state. Those who are lowly and enemies of the country will be deprived of their citizenship. He also quoted Hitler as saying: Only those whose parents are both of the Germanic race can be Germans and can be German citizens. Their bodies must be strong, their character must be pure, and they must be granted citizenship after completing their military service.

The citizenship law that Germany is about to promulgate has several characteristics, namely: German citizens must have strong bodies and pure character; they must serve in the military, obey discipline, and be loyal to the country and the head of state. I believe that anyone who understands the current situation in China and the general situation in the world, especially those of us who engage in the literacy education movement with the purpose of general knowledge guidance and civic training, should pay close attention to these points.

The Literacy Education Movement and the Police

— Cai Jinjun

The Republic of China has been established for twenty-four years, but it has not yet been able to become strong. Although there are many reasons for this, the most important is that the people are not enlightened and there are very few literate people. Therefore, the government's orders are mostly unknown to the majority of the people. Therefore, many obstacles have arisen in the implementation of government orders. How can a country not be weak if its government orders cannot be implemented among the majority of the people! Therefore, for the sake of saving the country and revitalizing the nation, Chairman Chiang believes that the work of promoting literacy education must be done first, completely abolishing the more than 80% of illiterate people in the country, and ensuring that all Chinese people can know how to write and read. Therefore, he recently issued a general order to the whole country to work together to abolish illiteracy. The central government has also decided that the central task for this year is to abolish illiteracy throughout the country. Mayor Wu has decided to start implementing literacy education in Shanghai on May 1st of this year, which has more meticulously and completely stipulated the implementation plan and supervision methods for us. Now, our only responsibility is to implement it on schedule according to the plan. Because the success or failure of this movement is very important to the strength or weakness of the country. The police represent the country in implementing all government orders, not only protecting the lives and property of the people and maintaining the peace and order of the country and society, but also actively assisting the development of all beneficial undertakings for the people, so as to achieve the most perfect state. Therefore, the police bear a major responsibility for this literacy education movement. I am now standing in the position of the police and offering three points of opinion as follows:

First, when starting the work of investigating the exact number of literate and illiterate people in the city, I sincerely hope that the leaders of all circles in the city and the general literate gentlemen will earnestly cooperate with our police and do their best to assist the illiterate people, indicating to them the methods and procedures for entering school and the important significance of the literacy education movement, so as to ensure that the investigation work and persuasion and propaganda achieve universal and broad effects in the shortest prescribed time.

Second, when we promote literacy education, we must follow a detailed plan, a complete plan, and formulate a daily literacy education schedule, earnestly implement it, and be meticulous in every detail, so as to make the effectiveness of the work better and better, and strive for perfection.

Third, we must be responsible for mutual supervision and assessment. Those who can fulfill their responsibilities, we encourage him and hope that he will fulfill his responsibilities even more. Those who do not fulfill their responsibilities, we must urge him to fulfill his responsibilities. If one urging does not listen, then urge again. If urging again does not listen, then urge three times, always demanding that the work of literacy education achieve the final goal in accordance with the prescribed plan. If it is really incorrigible and hopeless, we will very unceremoniously announce his name so that everyone knows. Because if there are really such shameless and bad elements in the group of human beings, not giving them appropriate punishment is not upholding justice. Therefore, in order to uphold justice, we must punish these negligent elements.

I believe that the above three points of opinion, although humble and without high opinions, feel practical. I hope that the leaders of all circles in the city, the general intellectuals, and all citizens will unanimously show the greatest determination and persevering perseverance to realize the central government's resolution on literacy education, Chairman Chiang's general order to promote literacy education, and the mayor's plan to implement literacy education under the leadership of our Mayor Wu, so as to ensure that all the people of this city can fully write and read in the shortest possible time, which is the foundation for saving the country and revitalizing the nation.

A Review and Prospect of Literacy Education

— Jiang Jianbai

The Attributes of Literacy Education: Some people ask whether the term "literacy education" is frequently heard. Regarding literacy as a category of education is considered inappropriate. Therefore, its attributes must be explained. Generally, formal schools such as primary schools, middle schools, and universities are considered education. A broader meaning includes social and cultural institutions, libraries, museums, etc., as education. In fact, according to a broad interpretation, all human activities and various forms of life are education and have educational value. Moreover, writing is a tool for recording human experience. How to read, how to understand the meaning of words, is undoubtedly an important form of education. Literacy is not just about recognizing the sound of words; the meaning of all words and the sentences formed by words are necessary processes in teaching. Therefore, literacy education includes common sense training, civic training, and the principles of being a person and doing things. Literacy education is the basic education of citizens, the initial literacy and education, and a part of what is called compulsory education. Therefore, in terms of the responsibility of the people, it is an obligation. In terms of national policy, it is compulsory. Literacy education is a comprehensive education that combines adult remedial education and children's compulsory education.

The Failures of Literacy Education: In the late Qing Dynasty, few people paid attention to literacy education. After the founding of the Republic of China, social figures gradually paid attention to it, either advocating the use of simplified characters or planning to use phonetic alphabets as tools for promoting literacy. The venues were either open-air schools, simplified character schools, public tutorial schools, or half-day schools, etc., as institutions for implementing literacy. At that time, it was difficult to achieve significant results due to the efforts of only a few people. However, the government did not have a concrete plan for the illiterate people of the former Qing Dynasty, so the effect was minimal. The concrete attention to the literacy movement and the start of publicity was the promulgation of the Outline of the Literacy Movement Propaganda Plan in 1929. The central government listed literacy as the top of the seven movements in the autonomous movement of the lower-level work of the Party at all levels, which also shows its special attention. In 1930, the Ministry of Education formulated and implemented a remedial education plan based on the resolution of the Second National Education Conference, which included literacy training and civic training, using the least amount of money and the shortest amount of time to enable the general public to read and write and have the ability to exercise their four rights. It is found that about 80% of the people in the country are illiterate. Assuming the national population is 436,094,953 people, a total of 348,875,962 people are illiterate. If those aged 16 to 60 who should receive remedial education account for about 46.5%, totaling 202,784,153 people, accounting for nearly half of the total population, plus about 60 million children who are out of school, totaling 280 million people who need to receive the minimum level of literacy education. Although the government has set various plans, due to the lack of funding and talent, and the implementers' ingrained habit of fearing difficulties and seeking ease, the huge number of out-of-school people remain as they were. With such a knowledge-lagging, rudimentary level of citizens, how can we expect to save the country from its declining danger!

The Conditions for the Success of Literacy Education: Literacy education is a major "task," and the responsibility for this major task still lies with "people." The reason why literacy education has not been successful in the past is "not that it cannot be done, but that it is not done." The reasons for not doing it are: first, there is a lack of mental construction, thinking that knowing is difficult and acting is not easy, so they sit and do nothing; second, there is a lack of self-confidence. Intellectuals often cannot believe how much ability they have. They are self-deprecating and decadent, how can they take on the responsibility of teaching people; third, there is a lack of practical spirit. People generally talk big and boast, but when they are really asked to do it practically, they cannot do it. This can also be said to be the failure of the essence of education in the past. Fourth, they do not pay attention to methods. Doing something is the goal. To achieve this goal, methods must be studied. Moreover, the complex and changing human environment is not immutable. Teaching illiterate people is several times more difficult than teaching in any formal school. If you don't think of ways from the psychological, environmental, and factual aspects, and say that it can't be done when you encounter failure, how can you succeed? Shanghai is a place with potential. During this period when literacy education is transformed from movement to implementation, everyone should be mindful of the man-made failures of the past where it was not that they could not do it, reflect on themselves, find the reasons within themselves, and not repeat the same mistakes. Therefore, success or failure depends on "people," so that everyone can work hard.

Post-literacy Education after the Initial Completion of Literacy Education: The increase in teaching experience lies in generalization and review. This literacy education is only the initial stage of popular education, which is far from the expected level of popularization. Therefore, after the completion of the entire first phase, there should be an entire second phase plan to continue implementation. After the completion of each phase of this plan (that is, after each phase of graduation), there should be itemized and categorized educational facilities, such as adding allusions to the words and texts that have been taught, and compiling popular picture publications, holding popular lectures and gatherings, and setting up literacy or question-asking places, all of which are indispensable work for generalization and practice. The former should still be handled by the government in a comprehensive manner, and the latter has to hope that the society will cooperate to promote it, so that the literacy education work can achieve practical results.

Review and Outlook of the Association's Work

— Tao Baichuan

This association was established on April 1, but officially started working on April 6. If we divide the periods based on important work as a standard, then April can be said to be the planning period, May and June can be said to be the preparation period, and after July can be said to be the implementation period.

As the Western saying goes, "A good beginning is half the battle." The importance of planning is certainly no less than preparation and implementation. Therefore, the work of the past twenty-odd days has almost exhausted our brains. Moreover, the large-scale promotion of literacy education is not only a pioneering work in Shanghai, but also in China. It is said to be unprecedented and with followers - because there is no precedent, we have nothing to learn from; because there are followers, we dare not be hasty, lest our failure shut the door to literacy education.

After twenty-odd days of hard work, we have finally established the entire plan. In terms of organization, we have established two systems: one is the general office of this association, with 22 district offices and 220 literacy schools and their 1,320 literacy classes; the other is the literacy education service team, with 300 sub-teams preparing to recruit 10,000 members as a supplement to the literacy schools. In terms of publicity, we have planned a publicity week, which is now actively underway. In terms of investigation, we are preparing to mobilize all the local police, household registration police, the education that has been admitted to the literacy school, and the older students from public and private schools in each district, to give full play to the spirit of labor service, and conduct a large-scale investigation of the illiterate people in the city. In addition, in order to test our ideals, we have set up two experimental districts, and now there are ten schools that can enroll students and start classes. The budget has also been prepared, with a total of about 170,000 yuan, of which the teachers' salaries and clothing expenses are estimated at about 110,000 yuan. The teaching materials are edited by ourselves. The content includes literacy education, common sense guidance, and civic training. The printing cost is very cheap, averaging only one cent and two and a half mils per volume.

The most important work during the preparation period is to investigate the illiterate people, followed by training teachers, followed by publicity, followed by enrollment and preparation for the start of school, and the completion of the literacy education service team is also one of the important tasks. The publicity has started on May 1 and will end on the 7th, but publicity among the people will still need to be continued in the future. The investigation work must be completed in three weeks, and will begin on May 14. The investigation committee in each district will be responsible for handling it. Based on the experience of the Jiangwan experimental district, the future results will be very impressive. Teacher training will be held after the completion of the investigation, and the time will be about three weeks. After the training, the teachers will be sent to each district to prepare for the start of school.

By July 1, most of the literacy schools in each district can start classes, and the members of the literacy education service team can also start looking for illiterate people to provide individual teaching, and the leaders of the sub-teams will be responsible for the collective training of the people; the work of this association will thus move from the preparation period to the implementation period.

The Central Mission of Literacy Education

— Chen Gongsu

(1)

Now is a world where intelligence is competing: the strength of a country's national power is directly proportional to the number of literate people in it. We can say that there is no strong country with few literate people, and in weak countries, education is always not universal, and the number of literate people is certainly small, because writing is the most important tool for acquiring knowledge. Those who recognize writing can use its power to seek knowledge and enrich the content of their lives. Those who do not recognize writing lose a way to knowledge, cannot get the development they deserve, and reduce the country's strength.

Our China, in terms of its vast territory, large population, and abundant products, should have dominated the world and led the nations. However, due to the harm of the foolish people policy and bureaucratic education for thousands of years, most people think that reading and writing is only a right and obligation that a few people should have. Therefore, the number of illiterate people in society is very alarming! It is estimated that the number of literate people in our China accounts for only 20%, and the remaining 80% or more are ignorant people who do not recognize writing. In this situation, the lives of many individuals, in fact, add infinite difficulties, and society is not easy to improve as a result. As a result, China has become a large but not strong country, suffering humiliation, not getting equality, and not being free!

Therefore, if we want equality and freedom for the country and the nation, we must seek to improve the knowledge of the people, so we must use rapid methods to carry out the movement to eliminate illiteracy. Now the city has decided to implement compulsory literacy education from July 3 this year, which is undoubtedly the most practical work to save the country. All citizens must do their best to promote its success.

(2)

Citizens have the responsibility to promote compulsory literacy education in the city to achieve the expected goals. The principle is clear. Therefore, in addition to the literacy education committee and educational administrative organs that are responsible for statistics, whether they are civil servants, freelance professionals, educators, all intellectuals, and various public groups, such as various general chambers of commerce, trade unions, associations, educational institutions, etc., really have a responsibility to assist the government in carrying out literacy education. Regarding the specific methods, they can either join the service team, or run their own literacy schools, or donate money and materials to run literacy schools. What is needed is that everyone recognizes the urgent need for this work and the responsibility that they should fulfill for this work and can do it practically.

We know that among the 80% or more of the Chinese people who are illiterate, farmers and workers account for the majority. Therefore, the target of literacy education is naturally the most important for farmers and workers. Based on this reason, we cannot but hope that there will be ample opportunities to implement literacy education in rural areas and factories. When we contribute our intelligence and financial resources, we must pay attention to this. We believe that in factories, trade unions and factories should jointly run it to achieve the effect of cooperation. If the area where the industry association is located is a commercial area and it is not easy to recruit students, it can contribute money to entrust the literacy education committee to establish schools on its behalf, and the name of the literacy school can be determined by the industry association that contributed the money. And each district's farmers' association and education association should at least set up one literacy school. The above is our general method of assisting the government. We can only make this great movement achieve twice the result with half the effort if we pool our efforts and cooperate fully.

However, what we want to mention here is the psychological construction of literacy education. As the saying goes: without knowing people, it is difficult to take a step; without knowing words, the world can be traveled. Although this is a popular view, its influence is enough to make ordinary people reduce their belief in literacy. Moreover, many people in society think that people like Ye Chengzhong and Yang Sicheng did not know words at first, and were able to achieve considerable success in society. They did not know that people like Ye and Yang had higher aspirations and perseverance than others. If they did not recognize words and had more knowledge, their success would have been even greater. Some people thought that since illiteracy can lead to fame, then whether or not literacy is important! Therefore, we must break this wrong concept in the publicity and persuasion of literacy education!

(3)

Speaking of the content of literacy education, it includes three parts: literacy education, common sense guidance, and civic training. The literacy education part includes the teaching of 600 words. These words are naturally not enough for the needs of life, and can only be said to be better than nothing. The imparting of common sense and the training of citizens are especially important. From a personal point of view, the central mission of literacy education can be said to be actually placed on civic training.

Our literacy movement is a movement to save the country. The reason why we want the people to be literate is to enable them to understand the great principles of saving the country, and then implement the "effective" work. Writing is just a tool for seeking knowledge. Our purpose is to let the people use this tool to obtain common sense of life, so as to increase their personal happiness. More importantly, they should receive civic training, understand the status of the country and the nation, understand the mission of our party, and understand the meaning of the Three Principles of the People, so as to take on the responsibility of the national revolution. Understanding this, then literacy education can give full play to its supreme role and have its supreme value.

(4)

In summary, we can know the importance of literacy education, our responsibilities and methods of assisting the government in carrying out literacy education, and the central mission of literacy education. At this eve of the First World War, our Chinese nation, which has a glorious culture, does not seek the continuation of its life. If we still intend to survive in the future, can we still follow the old ways and make mistakes, and not quickly wake up the people, strive to struggle and fight, in order to save the crisis of weak nations? Literacy education is a kind of work to awaken the people. I hope that comrades and compatriots who are determined to save the country will unite to complete this work, tightly grasp reality, so as to maintain the glory of the past and open up the bright future.

The Employer's Responsibility to Promote Literacy Education

— Ma Chonggan

Shanghai will eliminate illiteracy in the city from July 1. Implement compulsory literacy education for one year. Its significance is not a simple literacy education, but a national salvation movement that combines common sense guidance and civic training. All citizens should support it with all their strength.

The methods for promoting literacy education have long been detailed. If they can be handled in order, good results will be achieved. Now, based on what I have seen, I will put forward one thing for reference.

It is found that there are many apprentices and clerks in the city's shops and factories, and servants in families who are illiterate, or who know a little bit, but have not learned 700 or 800 words and have no common sense of citizenship. These people should receive literacy education. The managers of shops and factories and the masters of families should order them to enter literacy schools during their work breaks, or if it is inconvenient to enter school, the shops and factories can choose outstanding employees to serve as members of the literacy education service team and teach them at appropriate times. The servants in the family can be teachers by the master or children. Do not say that employees spend an hour a day learning to read and write and are afraid of hindering work, and do not let them receive the minimum level of education. Often know that after the workers are literate, they will deeply understand the great meaning and increase their ability. They will naturally be motivated to work, which will be beneficial to the nation, the employees, and the employers. If you don't believe it, please read the following facts.

In 1919, I participated in the May Fourth Movement and did my best to promote compulsory education, persuading the student unions of various schools and the joint associations of various business circles to open compulsory schools, and ordered the apprentices in the shops opened by the clan to study in compulsory schools. Unexpectedly, the manager objected on the grounds of hindering work, but I still insisted on letting them enter school. A year later, the apprentices increased their knowledge and improved their work. One of them has already been promoted to assistant manager and is capable of handling affairs. This shows a glimpse of the benefits of shops letting apprentices receive education.

The above is the fact that I have experienced. In this literacy education publicity week, it may be used as a reference?
