Sports News

The First Day of the International Games Chinese Preliminary Round; National New Record for Women's Javelin; Ms. Pan Yingchu Creates 32.29 Meters; Hao Chunde's Javelin is Very Good; Qian Xing-su's Performance Declines

The Chinese preliminary round of the Shanghai International Games was held at Zhongyuan yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock. A total of ten events were held in the men's and women's finals. In the women's javelin, Ms. Pan Yingchu threw three times in a row and broke the national record. The best result was 32.29 meters, which is far better than the old record of 27.75 meters held by Chen Rongming. Ms. Xu Yuan, who came in second with 27.93 meters, also exceeded the national record held by Chen. It was the most outstanding result of the day. Hao Chunde's 48.82 meters in the men's javelin was his masterpiece in his life, which is also rare. Ms. Qian Xing-su, the women's individual champion of the National Games two years ago, had no good results yesterday and fell behind. It is said that it was because she injured her foot playing basketball and has not yet recovered. In other events, Ms. Shi Ouqing's women's long jump result of 4.74 meters is also not far from the national record (4.88 meters).

Hao Chunde's Proud Masterpiece

Looking at the four men's field event finals, except for Hao Chunde's javelin, which was relatively satisfactory, the rest were mediocre. Tang Xianzhou, who came in second in the javelin with 47.44 meters, was also considered not weak. Gong Wanyu's 11.97 meters in the 16-pound shot put and Zhou Shunsheng's 11.93 meters in the second place were only barely satisfactory. Hao Chunde has degenerated in the long jump, and he was second to Wang He with 6.56 meters (Wang's result was 6.59 meters). The triple jump result was mediocre. Zhang Jia did not participate, which is inevitably disappointing.

Jia Lianren Has Unlimited Potential

In men's track events, there were few satisfactory results. Jia Lianren's 800 meters originally had the hope of breaking the national record. His strides were wide and his posture was very beautiful. He is indeed a rare talent in the middle distance. Unfortunately, he spent too much time in the first lap (the first 400 meters was run in 1 minute and 7 seconds (first)). Although he sprinted hard in the first lap, he only got 2 minutes and 9 seconds and 4 tenths. However, it is expected that he will be able to show his strengths in international competitions. Wang Zhenglin's 10,000 meters, 35 minutes and 4 seconds and 8 tenths, can be called the best in the country except for the old foreign man from Shanxi. He was exactly one lap ahead of the second-place Jin Zhongkang. Zhang Liang, who came in third, is a rising star in long-distance running. He has participated in various long-distance runs many times and his results are quite good. He competed fiercely with Wang Zhenglin in the first thirteen laps, not leaving an inch. Later, his strength was exhausted and he fell to third place, about 200 meters behind Jin Zhongkang. He Debao was first in the 400 meters, 56 seconds, which is very sluggish.

Shi Ouqing's Long Jump is Outstanding

Ms. Qian Xing-su, who holds three national records, participated in three competitions yesterday, but all fell behind. In the 50 meters and 100 meters, Qian was defeated by Li Sen, an unknown hero who came from behind, and both were more than one meter behind. However, Li Sen's results were not excellent. 7 seconds and 4 tenths in the 50 meters is equal to Chen Zaichun, who came in first in another group. 13 seconds and 9 tenths in the 100 meters. Chen Zaichun also belonged to another group, 15 seconds exactly, far inferior. Let's see if there will be any changes in the final tomorrow. In the final, Qian Xing-su's long jump was only third, and the result was much worse. Shi Ouqing's first place with 4.74 meters is rare.

Mediocre Results in the Preliminary Round

There were originally five men's track event preliminaries. Except for the middle hurdles, which were changed to be held tomorrow, the 400 meters and 800 meters were changed to the finals due to the small number of participants. The first place in the high hurdles originally belonged to Zhu Wenji, but was canceled due to falling four hurdles, and Tao Yingjie was promoted to first place, 17 seconds and 4 tenths, which is very sluggish. The results of the 100 meters and 200 meters were not good. Cheng Jinguan's absence was very disappointing. The veteran Hao Chunde only got 11 seconds and 9 tenths. Xue Jianqiu got 11 seconds and 6 tenths. Hao did not participate in the 200 meters. Dong and Xue were ranked first, and the results were mediocre.

Shanghai Handball Tournament Begins; Zhu Kuan Retains Championship Title

Kramer Second, Bao Shanli Third; Yesterday's Result: 2-0 Victory Over Kramer

In the Shanghai Sino-Western handball singles tournament, Zhu Kuan, with his outstanding skills and undefeated record, once again defeated Kramer in the final yesterday, maintaining his leading position among the heroes. The title of Shanghai handball king for this year still belongs to Zhu.

Final Standings of This Tournament

This is the second Shanghai Open Tournament. In the previous tournament, Zhu Kuan was the champion, Qu Keling was the runner-up, and Sun Daosheng was third. This year, Zhu Kuan is still the champion, Kramer is the runner-up, and Bao Shanhe is third. Last year's runner-up, Qu Keling, lost to Bao Shanli this time. Bao also lost to Kramer 14-21, 11-21. Third place Sun Daosheng retired from competition and did not participate.

How He Defeated His Opponents

Zhu always wins every match. The final match with Kramer was more promising. Kramer had suffered one defeat and needed to win twice to determine the outcome. Zhu only needed to win once to secure victory. In the first game, Kramer appeared nervous. Zhu took the lead with eight points, and Kramer gradually improved, but due to the disadvantage, he could not recover. Zhu's performance was so exquisite that he had unexpected skills. Zhu won the first game 21-13. At the beginning of the second game, the situation was tense. Kramer took the lead with 7-6 for the first time, but then Zhu Kuan took control, doing whatever he wanted. He had plenty of energy, handled the situation well, and hit every shot. His backhand was incredibly wonderful. Although Kramer lost, his results were still impressive. Zhu Kuan won the second game 21-11 and won this year's championship.

Chinese Football Mid-Level Group; Weihua Disqualified; For Using Unregistered Players in the Game; Fudan and Zhenru Tie for the Championship

The Chinese Football Association Committee held a meeting last night at Shen Garden to discuss the Fudan protest. The following decisions were made regarding this year's games: (1) Weihua team was disqualified from this season's game for using unregistered players and their previous scores were canceled. (2) This season's mid-level group games will no longer be held because it's too late. It was decided that the championship for the group would be shared by Zhenru and Fudan (same score). The league silver shield will continue to be held by the previous champion, Fudan, for another year.

Education News

Guangdong Province Revises Regulations for Selecting Students to Study Abroad

Based on the Ministry of Education's regulations for studying abroad and the proposal by Committee Members Chen, Zou, and Deng to strictly select government-funded students to study abroad, the Guangdong Provincial Government recently revised and passed the "Provisional Regulations for Selecting Government-Funded Students to Study Abroad in Guangdong," which consists of 25 articles. Key provisions are excerpted below: (Article 2) Guangdong Province's selection of government-funded students to study abroad emphasizes specialties such as science, engineering, agriculture, and medicine. (Article 4) Eligibility for application: (1) Graduates of public or registered private colleges or universities in China who have held technical positions related to their field of study for two or more years. (2) Graduates of public or registered private colleges or universities at home and abroad who have continued to study their field of study for two or more years and have valuable specialized works or other achievements. (3) Graduates of public or registered private universities or independent colleges at home and abroad with excellent academic records. (Article 6) Examination matters: The first examination is a physical examination. Those who fail cannot participate in the second examination. The second examination covers Party principles, Chinese language, Chinese history and geography, the language of the country of study (writing, translation, conversation), and three specialized subjects related to the applicant's desired field of study. (Article 9) Expenses: (1) Students studying in Europe receive 1,000 yuan for travel and clothing expenses. Tuition fees charged by the school are reimbursed in full each semester. The monthly living allowance is 14 pounds sterling. Return travel expenses are 40 pounds sterling. (2) Students studying in the United States receive 1,000 yuan for travel and clothing expenses. Tuition fees charged by the school are reimbursed in full each semester. The monthly living allowance is 75 US dollars. Return travel expenses are 300 US dollars. (3) Students studying in Japan receive 300 yuan for travel and clothing expenses. Tuition fees charged by the school are reimbursed in full each semester. The monthly living allowance is 70 Japanese yen. Return travel expenses are equivalent to two months' living expenses, to be pre-paid and then issued monthly by the overseas student management agency. Tuition fees for each semester will be remitted by the Education Department on a semester basis, and refunded after verification upon return to the country. (Article 11) The study period is limited to three to five years. Those with special circumstances who need to continue their research should report this to the Education Department for approval of the extended period. (Article 12) Unless there are special circumstances that have been reported to and approved by the Education Department, students may not change their field of study or country of study. Violators will have their scholarship revoked, be ordered to return to the country, and have all previously received expenses recovered. (Articles 13-15) During the study period, students must submit transcripts for the previous semester and a report on their research or internship activities (through the overseas student management agency to the Education Department for evaluation) before the start of each semester. If the report is not submitted within three months, the payment of educational expenses will be suspended. If the student fails two years, the payment of tuition fees and living expenses will be suspended. (Article 18) In the event of a major family emergency, students may apply to the Education Department through the overseas student management agency for leave to return to the country. The student may only depart after the Education Department has approved the leave. The duration of this leave shall not exceed one year. No tuition fees or living expenses will be provided during the leave, nor will travel expenses be provided. (Article 22) After returning to the country upon graduation, government-funded students studying abroad must provide service according to regulations. The service regulations will be determined separately. (Remaining articles omitted).

Chinese National Obtains Doctorate in Music in Germany for the First Time

Mr. Wang Guangqi

Mr. Wang Guangqi, who has been studying music history in Germany for many years, has made many discoveries in the evolution of Chinese and Western music and has written extensively. He recently obtained a doctorate from the University of Bonn in Germany, becoming the first Chinese person to study music history in the West. Mr. Wang went to Germany in 1919 and is currently a Chinese lecturer at the University of Bonn. He has written extensively on music, and his works have been published in China by the China Book Company.

A reporter from the Shanghai News Agency has learned the following details:

Ministry of Justice Replies: Difficult to Approve

Law students Luo Yiwen, Chen Zongli, Wang Zongshu, Shui Yunxiang, etc., from the China Public School of Law, received a reply from the Ministry of Judicial Administration stating that changes were difficult. The original letter is as follows: "The Minister has forwarded a letter from the Secretariat of the Judicial Yuan, requesting that students of domestic and foreign private universities have equal rights to participate in examinations, to comply with regulations and ensure fairness, and to investigate and reply to the matter. The temporary judicial official examination held by this Ministry this time is limited to graduates of law departments of national universities with scores above 80, as originally proposed by former Minister Luo for selection into the Judges Training Institute. The case has been submitted to the Executive Yuan and approved by the National Government. Changes are difficult. Those who have the qualifications stipulated in Article 7 of the revised Examination Law can participate in the higher examinations and judicial official examinations in the future, and should not have any regrets. This is a reply to Mr. Luo Yiwen, et al., from the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Judicial Administration."

Spring and Autumn

Drips and Drops

— (Boundless)

Fortune tellers, face readers, venereal disease hospitals... stand side-by-side, beggars, prostitutes… dense as stars, adultery, theft… news fills the eyes, this is the characteristic of Chinese cities.

Long hair, broken shoes, large bow ties, nearsightedness, today publishing a collection, tomorrow issuing a novel, this is the culture of Chinese cities.

Small bookstalls in the streets and lanes display all sorts of thin booklets, rented for women, children, and laborers to read; while singing "The seventh day arrives, crying mournfully," while peddling his small books, this is the education of Chinese cities.

Indian policemen confiscate the rickshaw puller's permit, foreign gangsters whip randomly gathered pedestrians, this is the authority of Chinese cities.

While singing the high tune of loving and using domestic goods, the body is wearing luxurious Western clothes, outwardly doing patriotic work, but in reality willingly being used by others, stipulating a women’s domestic goods year, the import of cosmetics has actually increased dramatically, this is the patriotic atmosphere of Chinese cities.

Discussion on Western Suits

— Zheng Yimei

About forty to fifty percent of people in Shanghai wear Western suits. In fact, wearing Western suits is more convenient and economical than wearing Chinese clothing. No wonder people are changing their attire one after another. I fear that in the near future, among men under forty years old, you won't find anyone wearing Chinese clothing. Speaking of convenience, whether going up or down stairs at home, or getting on or off vehicles on the road, there are no cumbersome problems. Even when traveling, just having a coat is enough. Speaking of economy, Chinese clothing includes leather, camel wool, lined,夹 (jia - lined but thinner than衬), single-layer clothing, which must be changed with the seasons. This clothing expense is considerable. As for Western suits, one set is enough for spring, autumn, and winter. In winter, just add a thick coat, and in spring and autumn, wear a light coat. Preparing summer suits is even easier. Some savvy friends even go to Wusong Road to pick up a suit for a little over ten dollars, and all the accessories are included. Walking down the street, they look proud and majestic, representing the new era.

However, the materials for Western suits are nothing more than wool and绒 (rong - velvet/fleece). These wool fabrics are entirely imported, and the money flowing to foreign countries is immeasurable annually. I remember that the year before last, when I was teaching a course at a certain girls' school, a very mischievous girl deliberately asked how to enrich the country. I replied without thinking, "First, the people of the country must not buy foreign goods." The girl then said, "Since that's the case, why do you wear a Western suit?" I was speechless. Fortunately, the class was over, so I pretended to be foolish and left. It's not that I don't want to use domestic materials to make Western suits, but when domestic materials are worn, in no time, the collar ends and the corners of the clothes will uncontrollably curl up, not conforming well. I sincerely hope that our country's industrialists engaged in textiles will work hard to research and improve, so as to recover our economic rights.

On the cuffs of Western suits, there are often several buttons without buttonholes. At one time, many people discussed their purpose, but the discussion yielded no results. I always feel that these are superfluous and can be removed. Also, the trousers of Western suits are always made very long, with a fold at the bottom, so as not to hinder walking. I think instead of folding, it would be better to make them shorter in the first place. Moreover, the fold accumulates dust and dirt, which is very unhygienic and has a hundred harms and no benefits. It would be better to abolish this style.

The Disillusionment of a New Family

— Hua Ling

Mr. Shen, who lived alone, fell in love with Ms. Yang in the autumn of last year. After half a year of courtship, they made a marriage vow to remain together until the end of time and held a formal wedding at a large restaurant, starting a small family life together. Mr. Shen was a noble person, and Ms. Yang was a high-achieving student. A perfect match, truly a match made in heaven. Everyone admired their blissful marriage.

After the wedding, they lived in great harmony, with laughter and music often coming from their room. But one night a month later, the music stopped, and the laughter was gone, replaced by the sound of the couple arguing. It only quieted down in the middle of the night. The next day, Mr. Shen went out early in a hurry to go to work, and Ms. Yang did not have the smile on her lips as she usually did.

According to their maid, the reason for their argument was a quick retort in their conversation.

A day passed quickly. In the evening, Mr. Shen came home very late. As soon as he arrived, the couple continued to argue. By midnight, they were fighting. Just as dawn was breaking, Ms. Yang went back to her mother's house in a fit of anger. As she left, Mr. Shen shouted angrily, "If you leave, don't come back."

A week later, the couple appeared in mediation court. Both sides had lawyers. Ms. Yang also presented a medical certificate documenting her injuries. After a period of mediation by the judge, under mutually agreed conditions, they signed the divorce papers.

From then on, Mr. Shen continued to live alone. He said, "Marriage is the graveyard of love!"

Naval Construction Competition

The Story of Gambling

— Zui Chi Sheng

Gambling is inherently a bad thing, capable of ruining families. But with good luck, it can sometimes help families prosper. However, this is rare and not to be taken as a model. Now, I will record two stories below, one of bankruptcy and one of rising from gambling, for readers' amusement.

In my hometown, there is a relative surnamed Jin. His family originally had hundreds of acres of fertile land. They also owned several buildings in a bustling area of the South City of Shanghai. But these properties have long since changed hands. It turned out that decades ago, on New Year's Eve, Mr. Jin's grandfather invited several relatives and friends for a New Year's Eve dinner. After the banquet, the host became excited and played dice with a close friend, Mr. So-and-so. They agreed to bet a certain property as a single, all-or-nothing wager. The property Mr. Jin wagered was the aforementioned buildings. As a result, Mr. Jin lost with a roll of the dice. The property was transferred and the surname changed from that point onward. Later, Mr. So-and-so, because he was good friends with Mr. Jin, stated that Mr. Jin would still collect some of the rent each year. At the time of his death, he even left a will instructing his descendants to abide by this arrangement. So, until now, Mr. Jin still goes to Shanghai every year to collect more than a thousand dollars in rent from the owner, and there is no contract. In the past, it was only several hundred thousand (coins), but as land prices rose, it increased to this amount, but it is still less than one-fifth of the current rent!

I used to live with a man named Hong, who was very poor. He worked in a domino shop, earning only a few dollars a month. It was impossible to think about starting a family and a career. One year, the end of the year arrived, and he got a few dozen dollars, which he took to a gambling den. He won repeatedly, winning two or three thousand dollars in a few days. So he used the money to marry a wife and start a family. He also partnered with several shareholders and opened his own domino shop. In recent years, all industries have been saying that the economy is bad. But his business has been doing well, with annual profits. People jokingly say to him, if he hadn't gone to the gambling den that day, how could he have had the qualifications to marry a wife and become a boss?

Little Western Heaven

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 12: Ashamed of Having No Clothes, I Lower the Curtain to Avoid Guests; Diligently Saving Lamp Oil, I Copy Books at Dawn

As soon as I entered, I saw another strange thing: three or four students were lying on the stone steps, writing with pencils. When I looked closer, I saw that they were copying someone else's copy onto their own. I asked them why they were copying books so early in the morning. He said, "By morning, the classmate needs his own copy, so he can't lend it to others to copy." I said, "Why don't you copy in the classroom?" He said, "The friends in the classroom are copying the formulas on the blackboard, and we're copying separately to avoid getting mixed up." I said, "You can also copy in your sleeping room." He said, "The room is too dark to see the book. And there are seven or eight people sleeping in the room, and there are only two benches and a small table, so not many people can sit." He wasn't lying. Some of them lived in cave dwellings, which were known to be dark. Those living in houses had small windows, covered with a piece of blue cloth, which was almost as dark as a cave. Because glass was a scarce item in the west, no one would use glass for their windows. As for using paper to paste the windows, unfortunately, there were too many windy days. Each gust of wind could tear the window paper to shreds. Zhou Yourong smiled and said, "You're exaggerating a bit. We in the east also have windy days, but it doesn't mean that window paper can't exist." Zhiqian said, "My county magistrate, you're in a place with trees, so you don't know that in places without trees, people save as much wood as possible when building houses. Their windows can't be like the windows in eastern houses, using fine wood to make tight window lattices." (196)

The Imperial Fragrance Drifting Record

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

However, the embroidery patterns here cannot be as diverse as those on shoes. They can only be limited to butterflies and bats. Other patterns may not be impossible to use, but if used, they probably wouldn't look very good.

I have already discussed the Empress Dowager's shoes and socks very clearly. As for how she wore them, it was the same as ordinary Manchus. The socks were about three or four inches higher than the shoe walls, and a soft silk ribbon was first tied tightly around the leg, then the trouser legs were pulled down and placed over the sock tops, and then tied with a silk ribbon. The color of this ribbon was always the same as the color of the pants themselves, mostly cut from a piece of the same material. This way of tying the trouser legs, as we think of it now, must be very unsightly, but in the past, everyone did it this way, so it didn't feel strange. Moreover, because of these two ties, not only would the socks never wrinkle, but the trouser legs would never come loose, so you would always feel very neat and tidy when moving.

Because so many phoenix shoes and satin socks needed to be made by the hands of the shoe-making women, this group of girls, although formally or in terms of class, were roughly the same as the palace maids in the palace, they were actually very different! Palace maids in the palace had no status. It could be said that they were inferior to the eunuchs. All kinds of hard work were their responsibility. They were simply busy serving others all day long, while the artisans not only did not need to serve others, but also had designated eunuchs to serve them! (306)

Places Visited

A Brief Account of the Ancient Site of the Confucius Forest

— Zhurong Shi

The Confucius Forest is where Confucius is buried, and it is also one of the ancient sites of Qufu. It is located three li outside the north gate of Qufu city. The Qufu station of the Jinpu Railway is built eighteen li away from Qufu city because of the Confucius Forest, fearing that the passage of vehicles would disturb Confucius's tomb. This is a sign of respect for Confucius!

After leaving the north gate of Qufu city, you can see a row of tall pines and cypresses, planted in an ancient and verdant manner on both sides of the pedestrian path leading to the Confucius Forest. This can also express the greatness of Confucius's learning. After passing two li of pine and cypress-lined path, a memorial archway-style gate appears, with the two large characters "孔林" (Kong Lin, Confucius Forest) written on it. This is the entrance to the Confucius Forest. Entering the gate of the Confucius Forest, short pink walls are built on both sides, planted with towering pines and cypresses, similar in size to those on the pedestrian path. Walking further in, there is Confucius's ancestral hall. Several pairs of stone carvings stand in front of the hall, which are necessary objects for ancient tombs.

At the place where you turn into the Confucius Forest, there is a "dismount stele." In the autocratic era, regardless of soldiers, civilians, or officials, they could no longer use horses or sedan chairs to travel in front of this stele. Confucius's dignity is fully expressed in this point.

Inside the Confucius Forest, what you see are many tombs of the Confucius family. A tombstone stands in front of each tomb, indicating the name of the person buried inside. The one in the center is exceptionally grand and majestic, and the tombstone is also particularly tall. This is naturally Confucius's tomb. The tombstone is engraved with the words "至聖先師孔宜王" (Most Sage and First Teacher, King Yi of Confucius). Those who admire the Confucius Forest naturally feel reverence when they arrive here, knowing that the greatest teacher of all generations, Confucius, is buried inside this tomb. The tomb in front of Confucius's tomb is the tomb of Zisi, the Transmitter Sage, who transmitted Confucius's learning. The rest of the tombs are all of the Confucius family. The most touching one is the tomb of the Restorer. The lineage of Confucius can be passed down to this day, with the Duke Yansheng lineage still existing, thanks to this meritorious official of the restoration, whose heroic deeds are still praised throughout Qufu.

After Confucius's death, Zigong guarded the tomb. This admirable deed has long been passed down. Behind Confucius's tomb, an earthen platform and several houses are built. A stone stele commemorating Zigong's tomb guarding stands on the platform. It can be known that this is where Zigong lived when he guarded the tomb. Zigong's hand-planted scholar tree was planted by Zigong when he was guarding the tomb. Today, it is completely dry. It is surrounded by iron rings and short walls, which only makes people feel a sense of history and becomes an ancient site.

Inside the Confucius Forest cemetery, there are countless towering pines and cypresses, which make the Confucius Forest even more solemn and ancient. Seeing the tombstone in front of Confucius's tomb makes people think of the greatness of Confucius's learning. It is not accidental that he became a teacher for all generations!

Publishing World

On Liang Shuming in Commemoration of the May Fourth Movement

— Li Maimai

"Eastern and Western Cultures and Their Philosophies"

By Liang Shuming, published by Commercial Press, price: 90 cents

Now is another period of re-evaluating the value of all past thoughts. If we should rigorously criticize even the relatively progressive intellectual leaders of the May Fourth era, such as Hu Shi, then we should not let the works of the backward thinkers of the May Fourth era, such as Liang Shuming, pass lightly. Moreover, Liang Shuming's works have now become the supreme scripture for the restorationists.

Liang Shuming's "Eastern and Western Cultures and Their Philosophies," ideologically, is an attempt by traditional Chinese thought to rejuvenate under the threat of modern thought; historically, it is merely a last burst of light from old China before the arrival of new China.

When China was entering the entrance to a new era, two Chinese with intellectual talent both attempted to use Western philosophy and science to rejuvenate and youthify the withered and aging traditional Chinese thought. One was Tan Sitong, the author of "Ren Xue" (Benevolence Studies), and the other was Liang Shuming, the author of "Eastern and Western Cultures and Their Philosophies." Although both of these people developed traditional philosophy from the same starting point, their historical significance is not without distinction; no, their distinction is extremely obvious.

If Tan Sitong's forcible and undigested attempt to youthify traditional Chinese philosophy with Western thought and science contained progressive significance, then Liang Shuming's similar work only has reactionary significance. If Tan Sitong's "Ren Xue" played a promoting role in the "Reform" movement of the time, then Liang Shuming's "Eastern and Western Cultures and Their Philosophies" is completely a reaction to the May Fourth New Culture Movement. Although Liang Shuming himself did not directly participate in the 利立 (Li Li) debate, Liang Shuming was the leader of the metaphysical aspect at the time.

In addition to the aforementioned internal reasons, the rampant decadent thought in Europe after the Great War was also one of the major reasons that prompted Liang Shuming to dare to make a fool of himself. Gu Hongming, Tagore, and even Liang Qichao were praised by Europeans at the time because Europe was in a critical condition, so Eastern thought in the form of ghosts and monsters was temporarily popular in Europe, which made Liang Shuming dare to issue the grand wish of using Eastern culture to save Western culture. We know that this in practice only made knowledgeable Europeans laugh at the Chinese!

Liang Shuming's fundamental error is definitely not, as Hu Shi said, that he should not have sought the "entirety" of Eastern and Western cultures; on the contrary, seeking the entirety of culture is the responsibility of thinkers who study culture. Because any culture is an integral whole, not a chaotic accumulation of cultural objects. Hu Shi's use of Chinese people's "eating rice" and "chopsticks" to oppose Liang Shuming's "setting a line" to understand Eastern and Western cultures is completely wrong.

Where does Liang Shuming's fundamental error lie? In his Eastern metaphysical method, in his Eastern metaphysical method of petrifying the changing, developing, and progressing Eastern and Western cultures and their philosophies, which can sometimes regress due to national or class reasons, into three unchanging, empty principles. This method is completely a reprint of Xunzi's thought of "the same principle remains constant throughout ancient and modern times," and is completely anti-historical and anti-scientific.

According to Liang Shuming, the fundamental spirit of Western culture is to desire to move forward. If Liang Shuming's words refer to European culture after the Renaissance, then how does Liang Shuming explain the more than a thousand years of stagnant European medieval cultural life? Also, Liang Shuming says that Chinese culture is intended to be harmonious, but when we examine the development of Chinese culture after the Qin Dynasty, it proceeds entirely along a curved line; it rises and falls, and after falling, it rises again. How does Liang Shuming explain this?

Liang Shuming's error lies in his treating the dominant thought of a specific stage of a particular society of a certain nation as the developmental principle of the entire cultural history of all nations. The so-called doctrine of the mean, which intends to be harmonious, is by no means a Chinese product. If Liang Shuming had read Aristotle's "Ethics," he would have known that Aristotle's doctrine of the mean is no less than Confucius's doctrine of the mean. The so-called doctrine of the mean is merely an expression of the reformist thought of the ancient aristocracy. What is so amazing about it?

The Western path of desiring to move forward, which Liang Shuming is so surprised by, is by no means unique to the West. This kind of thought, regardless of ancient or modern times, regardless of China or foreign countries, will inevitably be produced as long as there is the development of capitalism and the bourgeoisie. Weren't the ancient Indian materialists and the Chinese Yang Zhu and Han Fei all advocating the desire to move forward?

Furthermore, the desire to move backward is not a special product of India either. If Liang Shuming had studied the hermits in the Egyptian desert, the Stoics of Greece and Rome, and the Chinese Zhuangzi and Chen Zhongzi, he would know that the Chinese and Western desires to move backward are no less than the Indian ascetics. From this, we can know that the desire to hold the middle, move forward, or move backward are merely three different class psychological expressions of specific societies, and cannot be used as the permanent principles of the cultures of Chinese, Western, and Indian nations.

Although the above three principles can sometimes maintain their dominance in a particular nation, it is determined by the development or lack of development of the social economy, and is definitely not determined by these three abstract principles to determine the cultural form and lifestyle of each nation.

Liang Shuming's way of reversing cause and effect is entirely because he is an idealist combining Chinese and Indian thought!

Impressions of Various Bookstores

— Li Hengzhi

Commercial Press—China—World

(1) The Commercial Press—What is a bookstore? The Commercial Press—There are two groups of people who equate the common noun "bookstore" with the proper noun "Commercial Press." Before 1925, the Commercial Press was indeed second to none and regarded itself as the leader.

The angry tide of the National Revolution pushed the giant wheel of culture. The new book industry rose along with the new literature and new social sciences. On the Fourth Horse Road, bookstores sprang up like mushrooms. There was a time when progressive young people did not set foot in the Commercial Press except to buy textbooks. And the Commercial Press did not "follow the trend." Everyone said, "Hmph, the Commercial Press is declining!"

However, soon the situation changed. The Commercial Press watched as a large number of small bookstores closed their doors and went bankrupt, while it still stood firm.

On January 28th, the Japanese iron birds pecked and destroyed the entire Commercial Press. The enlightened textbooks of the World Bookstore tripled their profits during the Commercial Press's shutdown, and some even regarded themselves as successors to the Commercial Press. Everyone thought that the Commercial Press would be difficult to recover.

However, the Japanese iron birds did destroy much of the Commercial Press's material wealth, but at the same time, they also destroyed the Commercial Press's deeply rooted "relations of production" (forgive me for misusing this term). After resuming business, the Commercial Press made even more leaps and bounds on a new foundation. "The Eastern Miscellany" and "The Educational Review" once again occupied the top spot in magazine sales.

The Commercial Press... New Books Daily... Children's Library... Complete Library of the Four Treasuries! Wang Yunwu..." (The Commercial Press has once again become a giant in the book industry and the biggest threat to all bookstores.

(2) China Book Company—Almost as old as the Commercial Press. But we don't see anything intuitively, except for instruments and calligraphy. Yes, China Book Company's main profit-making items are instruments and equipment, except for the factory site property.

In terms of publishing, it is difficult to see what characteristics China Book Company has. At the height of the popularity of the new literature, China Book Company published the advertisement for the "China Literary Series" edited by Xu Zhimo. It wasn't until Xu Zhimo died and the trend of literary books had passed that we saw those few books come slowly. The "New China Textbooks" once sold well, but the Ministry of Education's "Temporary Curriculum Standards" became "outdated," and the set of books also faded away.

But, among many periodicals, we cannot but praise "New China" as being relatively progressive. Short and concise, and sometimes there are a few academic texts that are not in the "famous people's inscriptions" style, especially the past first volume.

(3) World Book Company—In terms of quantity and scale, World Book Company has invariably been in third place. In the past, when we mentioned World Book Company, we would think of Red House, Red Rose, Tales of Knights-Errant, and various love stories, sad stories, and guides, etc.

Soon, World Book Company made rapid progress, not only publishing many textbooks for primary and secondary schools (and often two books of each kind, which is even more characteristic), but also publishing many university textbooks of two or three hundred thousand words. There was a time when World Book Company and the Commercial Press were competing fiercely step by step. The Commercial Press had a university series, and so did the World Book Company. The Commercial Press had "New Books Daily," and so did the World Book Company. Sometimes, the World Book Company even surpassed the Commercial Press. For example, the "World Primary School Textbooks" in a certain year were rated higher than those of the Commercial Press and China Book Company by the so-called teachers' associations in certain places in the autumn semester.

However, many of World Book Company's characteristics are still unfathomable. Such as the World Bank, the Dahua Bookstore, and the World Publishing Cooperative, which are truly like a ring of stars, beyond the reach of other bookstores.

The change in the World Book Company's publishing direction was due to the triple profits of "ABC," but perhaps it is for this reason that people cannot help but feel a sense of "ABC" about the World Book Company's books, even the most profound university series.

Beyond the Art Exhibition Preview

— Zhang Feng

I finally saw the British-Chinese art exhibition preview at the old Bank of China building. Others said the items on display were second or third-rate, but I thought the bronzes and porcelains were quite good and worth seeing. Unfortunately, I was there with a large group of students, constantly giving instructions and answering questions, so I hardly had time to examine them carefully. They asked me two or three questions, and I could only answer one or two, which already took up half the day. I couldn’t be an all-knowing and all-understanding person, so I compromised and settled for being fifty-knowing and fifty-understanding.

"Mr. Zhang! Look at this 'Dwelling in the Fuchun Mountains' painting! Where is Yan Ziling's Fishing Terrace?" By chance, I had taken a trip there alone during the week-long spring break. Now that the famous painting was in front of me, I had to give it at least one glance. The so-called "brocade screen and embroidered peaks" of the mountain scenery were vaguely reminiscent, perhaps one or two out of ten. The most wonderful swirling eddies, the scenic spot of Seven Li 　, were not visible. I suppose the scroll was not fully unfurled and they were covered up?

Speaking of Yan Ziling's Fishing Terrace, here comes the question. Two large, square, fortress-like boulders stood on a mountainside seventy or eighty feet high. To say that one could fish there would be even more impossible than "climbing a tree to catch fish." How long would the fishing line have to be, and how big would the fish have to be? Many fools and poets are indulging their foolishness and writing their poetry in the "approximate but impossible" imagination. In reality, the answer to this question is quite simple:

Yan Ziling was a native of the Fuchun River, and it is possible that he lived in seclusion and fished there. However, there is also a Yan Ziling Fishing Terrace in Suzhou, so it must be taken into consideration – one cannot fish in only one place – why does fishing require a terrace? Why build such a pretentious mountain forest structure? Ultimately, it is because Emperor Guangwu supported him, and later generations also supported Emperor Guangwu, so they found a place to commemorate this great event, and the boulders were chosen for this purpose – the selection probably happened after Li Bai, because Li Bai's poem contains the lines, "Please leave the fishing line on the boulder, the fishing is about to end," which created this allusion – but there are two boulders – it wouldn't be impossible to give one to Xie 　yu as a souvenir.

Behind the "Dwelling in the Fuchun Mountains" painting is a scroll of the "Boundless Yangtze River," and the portraits of Emperor Taizu and Emperor Taizong of the Song Dynasty are also worth looking at and talking about. However, since I want to talk about things outside the exhibition, I can stop here.

Looking at the bronzes – as the saying goes, "Poor! Even if poor, there are still thirty-six thousand copper coins." Could this be a fitting inscription for the bronze room? I think the bronzes selected for the room are very good. My old friend Zhou Jinwen Cun, the author, Mr. Zou An, said so, which shows it is not just my personal opinion. From unearthed items to well-preserved items, one by one, group by group, with inscriptions and patterns, not ritual vessels, burial objects, or mortuary items, but rather containers, warming vessels, cooking utensils, and common utensils. Instead of the confusing so-called "dun," the ones identified by Guo Moruo as 　. This took up a lot of my time and effort, explaining and instructing the students, but since the conversation took place inside the exhibition, I can avoid repeating it here – but the term "common utensils" seems too broad and needs further consideration; perhaps this category is unnecessary. Among the so-called "common utensils," there is one item, number 82, a Panhui-patterned mirror, labeled as a Warring States period artifact. There is a pattern in the mirror, which is currently called a "four-in-one Ruyi" style pattern. Other artifacts with this pattern, such as the stone carvings from Lishi County in Shanxi, the gilded "four-in-one Ruyi" bronze pieces in our collection, and the fragments of small tin flower pieces, all match the pattern in this mirror. I have previously researched this pattern as Baosheng, Jinsheng, Fang Sheng, Hua Sheng, Cai Sheng, etc. Whether this pattern existed during the Warring States period has not yet been determined. Baosheng is one question, and Ruyi is another question, and they should be discussed separately. Regarding the Ruyi section, an Englishman named Hopkins wrote a long article in the 1923 "Bulletin," stating that it was transmitted from Buddhism. If we consider it to be Baosheng, perhaps we would not be constrained by Hopkins' discussion!

The bronze collection from Xinzheng – I was disappointed that the piece with the inscription "Prince Ying Ci..." was not selected. Looking at the craftsmanship of this bronze collection, the northern colors are still strongly preserved. After being unearthed, some people suspected that they were Chu artifacts that had spread to the Central Plains, but I am afraid not!

The bronze collection from Shouxian – number 106, the zu, is truly unprecedented. The cross-shaped pattern in the zu is probably not "for draining juice," as stated in the explanation. Perhaps it was used for smoking and roasting fish and meat? – Number 108, the square plate with a looped handle, has an inscription of nine characters, which is the same as the inscription on a broken dou in our collection – Number 105, the Chu King Kan Ken Ding, has an inscription of twelve characters, which is the same as the characters on the edge of the large bronze ding from Shouxian discovered in Shanghai in January of the twenty-third year. When the Shouxian bronzes were first discovered, I heard from Mr. Tan Tian that many were lost and not all were stored in the Anhui Library. The origin of the broken dou in our collection is a bit of a joke. I bought it from a Shanghai merchant named Sa on the evening of December of the twenty-second year, paid a fair price, and kept it for some time. However, when I played with it, I always had doubts, so I returned it and got my money back. A year later, I remembered the inscription and bought it again. Now, comparing it with number 108, the characters that I didn't recognize are still unknown. I don't know how Rong Geng identified the characters in his "Illustrated Catalog of Chu Bronzes," so I need to investigate.

Finally, I saw the two glass display cases of archaeological selections from the Academia Sinica. Unfortunately, the explanatory booklet had not yet arrived at the exhibition, so I will have to spend some more money to go back and review them. Among them, the bone axes and spearheads have already caught my attention, but I have not yet reached a conclusion. I will wait until I go back and look at them again before commenting.

Here is an excessive request: The Academia Sinica has conducted numerous excavations, but the number of publications is still limited. Why not hold a large-scale public exhibition so that people can also taste a forbidden fruit?

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Shortwave Components (Continued)

— Wang Shengshi

At high frequencies, the current tends to flow along the surface of the wire, so the plating on the coil must be carefully considered. Since silver is the most conductive metal, silver-plated wires have been used for shortwave coils. However, at radio frequencies, the conductivity of silver is only slightly greater than that of copper, so the latter is generally still used for wires. Enameled wire also has many advantages, the most important being that its surface remains bright and does not easily oxidize. If a large amount of high-frequency current passes through it, such as in the plate circuit of a commercial transmitter, a hollow steel tube should be used, coated with paint to prevent oxidation. This steel tube should not be nickel-plated, as experience has shown that this can increase the high-frequency resistance of the wire by about eight times. Conversely, tin-plating copper tubes does not affect their resistance. At the thickness of ordinary commercial tin-plating, the resistance only increases slightly.

In terms of installation, the coil should be wound tightly to prevent vibration during use, which can change the parameters of the radio. Ribbed coil forms, with appropriate grooves cut into them, can prevent this loosening. Alternatively, grooves can be cut into the form, and the wire wound inside the grooves. If plug-in coils are used, the pins at the bottom of the coil must be firmly attached to prevent them from loosening.

In a shortwave radio, the most troublesome source of loss is the tuning capacitor. This capacitor must have minimal loss, but loss can easily be introduced unless considerable care is taken in selecting this component. Sometimes its high-frequency resistance is even higher than the resistance of the coil it is paired with. In this regard, capacitors with air as the dielectric are the most suitable. Tuning capacitors with paper as the dielectric are completely unsuitable.

Like coils, when a tuning capacitor is connected to the circuit, some of the energy is dissipated within it. First, due to the true leakage loss between the plates, and second, due to the loss generated by the dielectric when the voltage changes.

Therefore, we can regard a tuning capacitor as a pure capacitance, where the current leads the voltage by 90 degrees, and a resistance R with no self-inductance is connected in parallel with it (Figure 2a).

From mathematical calculations, we can transform this parallel resistance R into an equivalent series resistance r, which is inversely proportional to the square of the frequency. At high frequencies, the value of r is extremely small, so we know that most of the loss is absorbed by the dielectric.

The tuning capacitor should have as little dielectric supporting the plates as possible, and this dielectric must be suitable for high frequencies. The metal plates should be made of copper, and each group should be securely fastened. This is very important, because shims are commonly used to fill the space, and if the shims oxidize, the effectiveness will be reduced. The capacitor's rotating shaft must not wobble to avoid noise during rotation.

(3) Tuning Capacitor Values and Other Considerations

To avoid overcrowding the radio spectrum, the capacitance of the tuning capacitor should not be greater than 100 picofarads, i.e., 0.0001 microfarads. The ratio of its maximum to minimum capacitance should be as large as possible, so that the same coil can be tuned to a wider range of wavelengths.

In Figure 3, C and L are the tuning inductance and grid capacitance, and 　 and 　 represent the capacitance between the leads and between the filament and grid. 　 is approximately equal to 5 picofarads, and 　 is approximately equal to 8 picofarads. 　 and 　 can both be considered as being connected in parallel with C.

If a precisely designed capacitor is used as C, with a capacitance of 100 picofarads, then its minimum capacitance is only about 5 picofarads. So the ratio of maximum to minimum capacitance is 183/13, approximately equal to six to one. Using a fixed inductance, the tuning range is approximately two and a half to one. We assume that the tuning range is from 20 meters to 50 meters.

Now, if we use a poorly designed capacitor with a minimum capacitance of 20 picofarads, then the ratio of maximum to minimum capacitance is only 113/33, or 3.4 to 1, reducing the range by almost one point eight to one. So, using a much smaller inductance than before, we can only tune from 20 to 36 meters. Smooth tuning is very important for shortwave reception, and a specially designed dial is used to control it.

Fixed capacitors are no different from those used in broadcast radios, but those with low loss must be used.

Variable coupling can also be used, but this type of coil must be designed with appropriate skill. The contact points must be clean to prevent noise during reception or an increase in resistance after prolonged use. Figure 4 shows a highly effective variable coupling method. Note that the primary, grid, and feedback coils each have several taps that can be matched. This type of coil must be carefully designed, otherwise dead spots may occur, at which points no oscillation can occur.

The pins and base of plug-in coils should have good contact, and the dielectric used for insulation must be suitable for high frequencies. The distance between the pins of the base should be as large as possible to reduce leakage loss.

The inductance of a high-frequency choke coil should be very high, and its self-capacitance should be very small, while its external field should also be very small. Because this type of coil is used to block high-frequency currents in the circuit, a capacitor is also used to shunt this current to ground. To obtain a very high inductance and very small self-capacitance, this choke coil is usually wound in sections and then connected in series. In this way, the inductances are still additive, but the self-capacitance is reduced to a very low level due to the series connection. If the radio components are tightly packed, the choke coil should be shielded to limit the generated electric field.

The dial of the tuning capacitor is very important for reception, so it must be of the slow-motion type. Some amateurs even use a ratio of 100 to 1, but in general, a ratio of 15 to 1 is sufficient.

The effectiveness of the radio also depends on whether the regeneration control is appropriate. The capacitor used for control must be free of noise, and it is best to use slow-motion tuning as well. This is even more important for receiving distant radio signals. (End)

Introduction to the 6A7 Pentagrid Converter Radio

— Qi

The special feature of this radio is that it uses a 6A7 pentagrid converter tube to perform both detection and audio frequency amplification. The former is performed by the tetrode section, and the latter utilizes the oscillator grid and plate sections. The design is very economical, and the results are quite impressive. Listening to local radio stations through the speaker is already satisfactory. At maximum volume, it is approximately equivalent to an ordinary three-tube radio. The selectivity is also quite good. The components are kept to a minimum, and the assembly is compact to make a small and exquisite pocket radio.

Power Supply – This radio uses a 7Z3 for direct power supply type half-wave rectification to provide the 6A7 plate voltage. The filaments of the two vacuum tubes can be connected in series and then connected to the ×× point of the 220V input line via a resistor R3. If you want to be more economical, you can make it a semi-AC type: you only need to find another power transformer with a 6V output on the secondary side to light the 7A7 filament: the B power can be replaced with a 135V dry cell. In practice, the same results can be obtained.

—List of Parts—

LLrL — 1 inch bakelite tube L wound with 20 gauge wire for 4 turns, spaced 2 points, Lr 30 gauge wound for 80 turns, spaced 2 points, L same gauge wire for about 40 turns

CC1——0.00035 MFD small mica insulated variable capacitor

C2——0.002 MFD fixed capacitor (to prevent C1 from short circuiting)

C3——0.00025 MFD grid capacitor

C4——5 or 1 MFD fixed capacitor (must be voltage resistant to 1000 volts)

C5C6——5 MFD fixed capacitors

C7——8 MFD electrolytic capacitor

C8——2 MFD fixed capacitor

R——3 MFD resistor

R1——2500 ohm carbon resistor (better if wire wound)

R2——50,000 ohm potentiometer

R3——670 ohm fixed resistor

T——3:1 audio frequency transformer

A,F,C——30 Henry audio frequency choke

Method for Converting Regenerative Radio to Automatic

— Cao Runsheng

A regenerative radio cannot perform at its full potential when regeneration is either too little or too much. If too little, the volume is not high; if too much, only howling is heard and the audio is overwhelmed. The key to automatic regeneration is to adjust the regeneration at the same time as the wavelength, combining two steps into one.

Originally, many radios used a capacitor to control regeneration, so if we used a dual variable capacitor to control the wavelength and regeneration, wouldn't that make it automatic? However, while the theory is correct, in practice, the capacitance of the capacitor used to control regeneration is too large. Because the maximum capacitance of ordinary dual variable capacitors is mostly 0.00035 or 0.00036 MFD, this is suitable for controlling the wavelength, but it is too large for controlling regeneration. When used, one will definitely feel that the regeneration and wavelength cannot be synchronized. Therefore, we also need to connect a fixed capacitor in series to reduce the capacitance. According to the author's experimental results, a capacitance of 0.001 MFD is most suitable. From DC single-tube radios to AC four-tube radios, stable regeneration can be obtained in each wavelength band, and many friends have also tried it and found it to be most suitable.

The circuit diagram above is used on a most common single-tube radio, and it can be similarly installed on various radios. This is just an example!

When using it, first pay attention to the radio station with the shortest wavelength, gradually move the regeneration coil closer to the secondary coil, making the maximum volume about to oscillate but not yet oscillating, then move it back slightly and fix it. In this way, the wavelength and regeneration can be adjusted simultaneously, and it is very stable. Amateurs might as well give it a try.

Conversations

Moscow Cracks Down on Street Beggar Children

— Xing'an

A National News Agency dispatch from the 24th reports that Moscow municipal authorities have recently launched a large-scale crackdown on street beggar children in the city. These beggar children wander everywhere, and their situation is extremely pitiful, having become the most serious problem in Soviet Russian society. It is said that in the past three weeks, Moscow police have searched everywhere and arrested 1,202 homeless children. Some of them have had their parents' residences located, and they were immediately sent back home and their parents warned that they have a responsibility to support their children. As for cases where parents were reprimanded by the police for neglecting the lives of their children, there were as many as 11,300. Street beggar children who are arrested and whose families cannot be found are sent to public institutions to be raised.

From the above facts, we can see that the internal society of Soviet Russia, which practices communism, still has many defects. First, Soviet Russian society is a communist society. However, in this communist society, there are still so many beggar children wandering everywhere, without clothing or food, and their situation is extremely pitiful. This must be said to be one of the biggest defects of communist Soviet Russia, and it is no wonder that it has become the most important problem in Soviet Russian society. Second, in Soviet Russian society, the general public has become more sexually liberated, which has led to a weakening of family concepts and a growing estrangement in the feelings between parents and children. As a result, more than a thousand homeless children and more than ten thousand cases of parents being reprimanded by the police for neglecting the lives of their children have been created. This is also a defect of the communist country of Soviet Russia.

What would these unfortunate children abandoned by society on the streets of Moscow think if they knew that the society they were standing on was a communist country?

Plum-Flavored Mood

— Qin Jian

In the season when people change into light, thin shirts, the air also begins to have clouds floating around like vagrants in the human world: diverse, and ever-changing. At that time, without inquiring into the records of the season, everyone understands: what is unfolding in this vast world is no longer the purple, dreamlike spring, but: May, with one or two green plums dotted in the red flower bushes – May brings many alarming unpleasantnesses, and also brings the sour taste that calls to mind the poems of the cuckoo.

(Really, I can't think anymore, I can't think anymore. Every year, when people in the streets show a lighthearted attitude in their spring shirts, and a sharp voice of a plum peddler floats in the deep, long alley, I have already lost the function of thinking, and only a sickly heart remains, panting and dying.

—It's plum-flavored time again. The green sourness will only bring people a kind of painful remembrance of the lost past. But this is only a torment, a punishment, for a person who is not suitable for leisurely thoughts.)

Thinking: When the plums ripen, it will be the time for my own child to go up to the trembling cross of life.

I have already lost the sense of time and space: the only thing I can remember is an image of childhood that emits a silver-flower-like, brilliant light; on it exists the smile of beloved humanity, the sunlight-like, clear heart of the same year, and the orchards dotted in the holy little village (I started to know the plum tree there, and I also started to see her who has already been buried in the pit of memory.) The familiar but not luxurious large rafters in front of the old family gate, the crow's nest residing under the eaves, and many bucolic midsummer evenings.

(But now, this small, peaceful world has been completely destroyed: destroyed in the flames of war, destroyed in famine, destroyed in my own long wandering days...

In the brown-gray memorial, even the most desirable plum flavor and her grass-green voice, make people afraid to think about it.)

The peaceful family house has faced countless storms in the alternation of the times, and the result of poverty and suffering repeatedly attacking the aging generation has finally brought down the fate of the entire generation, just like the plum trees in the orchard. Carrying a small plum-flavored heart, I was pushed out of the peaceful countryside, thrown into the sea of ​​life, drifting and struggling.

However, my child was grown up from the quiet fields, from the plum flavor in the beautiful orchard, from the simple world; and there, I still retain the soul of childhood, and the indelible, gauze-like smile.

When I think of the vast road of life like the sea, the young soul has already lost the courage to live. What I remember is that it was on a May night when the plums were ripe, at the car exhibition in a small town, she said one sentence to me: "Don't pour the sour taste of plums into your heart, the history of life needs courage. When a good era comes, maybe we can come back to see the fullness of the plums."

Yes, the days of suffering will not be without end, "maybe" there will be a day when I will see the leisurely sky of my hometown and the plums in the orchard again?

In that case, I am always living day by day with a plum-flavored mood in the remembrance of the past, and May, which is regarded as a moving season, passes in suffering again and again with the plum flavor. The good days are infinitely far away—perhaps they will flow away forever behind people's backs.

Early Summer in the Park

— Ai Tu

I. Morning

In the morning, before the sun comes out, the city is still shrouded in a faint, smoky rosy cloud. The streets are quiet, and gusts of cool, late spring wind blow against the chest, still carrying a hint of lingering cold, making people feel that the weather at this time of year is so abnormal.

Stepping into the park, at this moment, apart from the whistling sounds of the wind swaying through the dense treetops and the little birds chirping incessantly with a completely joyful air, seemingly unaware of the desolation or sorrow of the human world, everything is quiet. Most of the people in the city are still in sweet dreams, and the park is covered by an indescribable cool curtain.

The sun, the gentle early summer sun, seems to be like a beautiful and shy girl in her adolescence, smiling coyly as it emerges. The universe is dressed in a vast, bright red veil-like garment. The sunlight climbs onto the lush green treetops, and the birds are singing joyfully, as if celebrating their happiness. The sun gradually moves from the tall treetops to the peaceful meadows, shining on the tranquil lake surface. White spring water pours down the lakeside rocks, gurgling into the lake. The lake surface is also reflected by the red light of the rosy clouds, making even the green shadows of the drooping willows appear particularly beautiful. Countless goldfish swim and frolic on the water surface, creating circles of tiny ripples. Here, everything in the morning park is so beautiful and lovely.

II. Happy People

Gradually, the park is adorned with a continuous stream of visitors, with no more tranquility, no more birds singing, and no more lingering cold – the park is filled with the scent of early summer everywhere. From the moment the sun's light turns white and gradually hangs high in the sky, until dusk when the sun seems to breathe wearily as it sets in the west, the park is noisy, with no trace of tranquil poetic charm. What the eyes can see, apart from the colors of the lush green trees, are groups of women dressed in spring and summer clothes, made up so charmingly, and the debauchery of young men. In the distance, people are chasing after such crowds. Ah! This is a time filled with the intense scent of youth! Young people are all equally moved by the adorable and beautiful shadows.

Apart from the whispers of young couples, apart from the faces revealing the thirst of the times, and apart from those who seem oblivious to the bleakness of the era, reveling as if in a frenzy, we can see groups of children wearing beautiful red and green clothes playing and chatting on the beach, running on the verdant meadows, their joyful mood adding infinite color to the park.

III. Dusk

The sun must truly be tired, having hung in the high, azure sky for so long. Now, it gently disappears behind the treetops. A desolate red sunset, a scene truly different from the morning's atmosphere, gradually departs from the human world.

Groups of people gradually leave the park. When the pitch-black night occupies the universe, the park reveals a terrifying, unclear, and blurred picture, vast and expansive. Poets should be writing poems under the lamplight in their houses, and revelers in the city should be turning upside down in sweet dreams.

But alas! The park is as if dead, with no sign of youth.

Returning Home at Night

— Especially

The night is still, the sky is still, and the air is still.

Saturday night, a day deeply etched in one's heart, a day that stirs excitement!

The standard clock on North Sichuan Road tells you it's already 3:15. Green clouds, pregnant with impending movement. Drunken sailors, humming disorderly tunes. Aren't they? The red lights are eerily glaring. At some point, you might find them annoying, but at this moment, on this unforgettable Saturday night, they seem to possess a different kind of power, piercing into everyone's eyes. The differently colored words above the doors of taverns and dance halls especially compel your weary heart.

Once past the Sichuan Road Bridge, you can't help but relax your excited mood. There, you find no stimulation, and what you encounter is only dead silence.

Time runs incessantly. In front of the Huiluo Company, the road lying across is like a snake, resting peacefully, its back oily black, emitting lazy light.

Risen Sun Building, such a familiar name. Intersecting train tracks crisscross. Several anxious cars constantly ask, "Taxi, do you need one?" This inevitably becomes annoying to those who are used to walking. The atmosphere of depression surrounds every heart. Under duress, he can't help but ask, but who can understand? Even those with relatively decent attire are suffering the same pain, constantly struck by this suffering.

A small shed, close to the train tracks. Several small red lights are placed separately, the firelight projecting around the shed, a grand spectacle!

Legs, a little sore. Heels, swollen! Is it inhumane? Finally, the taxi pulls me away. The driver's legs, so strong. The taxi runs on the snakelike road, so crisp! In the quiet night, the sound waves easily rush into your eardrums.

A bend, a road, passes quickly. Kissing the chilling wind, it turns into a street with exotic flavor. Straight and upright, the lights are neither too many nor too few, the brightness just right. The circles of light cast on the smooth road are very round. The trees on the sidewalk, sprouting verdant leaves, are assaulted by the wind, rustling softly.

Unconsciously, my eyes closed, my body bumping along with the driver's footsteps. Gradually, a layer of chaos wells up in my heart, my consciousness beginning to blur.

"Suddenly," the taxi stopped. Sweat beads streaming from his forehead. Needless to say, his face was flushed red. He looked at me, giving a knowing smile. I touched my pocket, added a few more coppers, rubbed my eyes, and thought to myself:

—Ah, another day has been whiled away.

Page 21

Spring at the Inn

— Ke Ming

Although it is said that the times have moved with flying steps to the cutting edge of the twentieth century. The twentieth century, in prosperous metropolises, is said to be a world of machines, a world of electricity, and a world suitable for enjoyment and convenience! It's spring, and there we can imagine: streamlined, high-speed automobiles speeding along glass-smooth streets; mechanical boats racing in the water like a line; the metropolises of the twentieth century, even the natural objects in the wild – this blue-purple mist-shrouded mountain, this stream as soft as a girl's affection – have all been washed by science: only there does true modernity, the true twentieth century, reside.

Really! If you, like us, were to visit some of the impoverished and ancient villages located in the remote north, hire a skinny nag, and walk wearily on the endless, long, and desolate sandy road for an entire day, until the sun is setting (at which time, the prosperous metropolis is just beginning to bustle), fearing bandits and wild dogs on the dark road, you would have to quickly find a dilapidated and ancient inn to settle down, and then, under the light of the oil lamp at night, listen to the old sighs and sorrows of various people. You would surely forget the progress of the times and have a medieval feeling of desolation.

Under the drifting nature of business, we once again agreed to make a long-distance tour. When we left, it was a picture-perfect spring in Jiangnan; there were brocade-like flowers, and people as beautiful as flowers, but in this good season, we carried cloth, medicine, Mei Foo lamps, sugar, soap, and other daily necessities, drifting aimlessly to this remote small village in the north.

It was already the picturesque third month of spring! But there, we still felt the biting, desolate wind; on a dim evening, several people sat in sedan chairs, slowly walking on the silky-smooth sandy road. That kind of image is difficult to describe; and then, dusk fell as quickly as lightning. When the distant bald mountains turned into ghostly black shadows in the vastness, we had already found a place to rest in the "Bao Family Old Inn," marked with "Officials, Merchants, Guests, Welcome," and were drinking cool spring wine under the only few yellow-tinged-red Mei Foo kerosene lamps in the entire village.

The inn was the most elaborate in the village, even more so than "Bao Family's": people gathered in a large, undivided room called the "guest hall," where the brick bed had no fire underneath, because it was spring. Yes; the weather warmed up, and there was less fire on the brick bed, but the room had more of an unpleasant musty smell. That kind of smell constantly smoked people, and people would have a disgusting discomfort. Two kerosene lamps hanging on opposite corners of the room emitted black smoke on one side, while emitting a dull yellow light on the other, illuminating the wine-flushed faces of the guests. People gathered in twos and threes under the lamps, playing paper-cutting games, lamenting the hardships of old age, talking about famine years, discussing the harvests of wheat and sorghum, and talking about the market prices of bird's-eye satin...

Containing unclear voices numbed by the burning liquor, what was represented were all the dissatisfactions of the locals and outsiders, cursing, sighing, arguing; mouths moved, and hands moved too. Another night came in turmoil; it is difficult for people to be stable in suffering, just like a wildfire in the north wind.

But when half the kerosene in the lamp burned out, and the light went from dim to extinguished, the people all lay scattered on the ground, snoring messily. A gust of wind swept through the paper window: the third month of spring in the north carried a musty smell, like a rotten Middle Ages...

Yuanchang's "Meow Meow Collection" Issue 14 Published

The Shanghai Yuanchang Advertising Company Radio Station has been publishing the "Meow Meow Collection" monthly magazine for fourteen issues. In addition to content such as songs, opening essays, and novels, it has recently added the latest programs from more than ninety radio stations across the country. Movie News

Lianhua News

"National Style," which the Chinese people eagerly desire, is Lianhua's biggest film of the year. Written by Luo Mingyou and co-directed by Luo Mingyou and Zhu Shilin, it is Ruan Lingyu's last masterpiece before her death. This film will be released soon.

Sun Yu has decided to adapt "The Admirable Crichton" as his new work after "The Big Road," but he intends to change the title to "Go to Nature."

"Tianlun" (Grand Destiny) is Lianhua's most ambitious special production of the year. Naturally, the completion of this film requires a lot of money and time.

Lin Chuchu has been very busy lately. The work on "National Style" has just finished, and there are still many scenes to be filmed for "Tianlun," and now she is also acting in Wu Yonggang's "Little Angel."

Li Lili and Luo Peng are the best dancers and have made great contributions with their "feet" in "National Style."

Wang Renmei said to George, the director of "Little Angel," "We will be filming sound films soon, so you should quickly learn Mandarin." He said, "I won't learn Mandarin, I will learn the national language."

Cai Chusheng is preparing to write for Lianhua's newspaper and magazine for a long time. His "A Day's Dream of the Windy Pavilion" collection will be published continuously from the fifth volume, tenth issue onwards.

Because Lianhua is concentrating on film production, expanding the photography studios, and increasing the number of directors, a new strong general has joined the directorial team. He is Wang Cilong, who has a long history and great achievements in the Chinese film industry.

Yang Xiaozhong said: "'Four Sisters' are four women with different personalities. Their experiences are also different."

While filming Luo Peng's engagement and betrothal in "Cold River Setting Sun," it rained heavily. Diao Banhua braved the rain to offer his congratulations.

All of Lianhua's work is very intense, and the translation department is also editing the "Lianhua Yearbook" for 1934.

"An Ill-Fated Marriage" starring Helen Hayes and Montgomery is playing in Nanjing.
